Public Comment 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
             PUBLIC COMMENT PROCEDURES 
 
The Southern Pines Town Council is committed to allowing members of the public an opportunity to 
offer comments and suggestions.  In addition to public hearings, a special time is set aside for the 
purpose of receiving such comments and suggestions.  All comments 
and suggestions addressed to the Council during the Public Comment Period shall be subject to the 
following procedures: 
 
1.   The Public Comment Period will be held at the end of the Council Meeting. 
 
2.   Each person choosing to speak is asked to keep their statements to a reasonable length in time in 
recognition that others may also wish to speak and that the Council requires time to conduct its 
normal business.  The Chair retains the right to limit discussion as he/she deems necessary. 
 
3.   Speakers will be acknowledged by the Mayor/Chair.  Speakers will address the Council from 
the lectern at the front of the room and begin their remarks by stating their name and address 
for the record. 
 
4.   Public comment is not intended to require the Council and/or staff to answer any impromptu 
questions.  Speakers will address all comments to the entire Council as whole and not one 
individual member.  Discussions between speakers and members of the audience will not be 
permitted. 
 
5.   Speakers will be courteous in their language and presentation.  Matters or comments which are 
harmful, discriminatory or embarrassing to any citizens, official or employee of the Town shall 
not be allowed.  Speaker must be respectful and courteous in their remarks and must refrain from 
personal attacks and the 
use of profanity. 
 
6.   Any applause will be held until the end of the Public Comment Period. 
 
7.   Speakers who have prepared written remarks or supporting documents are encouraged 
to leave a copy of such remarks and documents with the Clerk to the Council. 
 
8.   Speakers shall not discuss any of the following:  matters which concern the candidacy of any 
person seeking public office, including the candidacy of the person addressing the Council; 
matters which are closed session matters, including but not limited to matters within the 
attorney-client privilege, anticipated or pending litigation, personnel, property acquisition, 
matters which are made confidential by law; matters which are the subject of public hearings. 
 
9.   Action on items brought up during the Public Comment Period will be at the 
discretion of the Council.

To: 
Reagan Parsons  
Via: 
BJ Grieve, Planning Director 
From: 
Lauren Long, Planner I  
Subject: 
CU-03-19 and S-48-19: A Conditional Use Permit and 
Major Subdivision Preliminary Plat for 58 Lots Within 
an Existing Residential Development; Applicants: 
Plantation Investors, LLC (Bob Levy); Bob Koontz of 
KoontzJones Design PLLC, Authorized Agent 
Date: 
June 9, 2020 
I.
SUMMARY OF APPLICATION REQUEST:
Mr. Bob Koontz has submitted an application for a Conditional Use Permit and a
Preliminary Plat for a major subdivision of 58 total lots on 23.64 acres zoned RS-2CD.
The proposed subdivision is within an existing residential development presently called
“Mid South” that was approved in 1988 for 647 dwelling units. The development is
located on the east side of Knoll Road between  Midland Road to the north and Morganton
Road to the south. The preliminary plat is for two phases. Phase One will be located along the
extension of Plantation Drive south of Claret Court and proposes 52 single-family lots along
with open space. Phase Two proposes six single-family lots and one lot dedicated to open
space east of the intersection of Plantation Drive and Hadley Court. The subject parcels are
identified as PIN: 857200543226 (PARID: 20120323) and PIN: 857200614866
(PARID: 20071162). Per the Moore County tax records, the property owner is listed
as Plantation Investors, LLC.
II.
PLANNING BOARD ACTION:
At the May 21, 2020 Regular Meeting of the Planning Board, in accordance with UDO §
2.5.2, the board voted to observe the procedures defined in UDO § 2.13.2 for Legislative
Public Hearings. The Planning Board heard from staff as well as those in attendance
regarding application CU-03-19 and S-48-19. Planning staff presented a review of the
Conditional use Permit application for a Major Subdivision and Preliminary Plat. Planning
staff reviewed details of the project and discussed compliance with the Unified
Development Ordinance (UDO). Staff noted that the applicant would need to request
deviations based upon their application submittal to the street cross sections and specify
the built standard they were seeking.
Mr. Koontz presented a slideshow presentation and answered a variety of questions from
the public and the Planning Board. The Planning Board asked about the future connection
of Plantation Drive, circulation and access of traffic for construction and emergency
vehicles, stormwater requirements, the security and adequacy of the proposed emergency
CU-03-19 & S-48-19 Midsouth East End
June 2020 Town Council
Page 1 of 140
access road, and about landscape buffers between the perimeter of the proposed 
subdivision and the existing surrounding development. Mr. Cliff Dahl, who resides at 115 
Belfair Court, asked about the connection and loop of Plantation Drive and expressed his 
concerns about access due to the limited number of existing access’. Mr. Dahl explained 
that he had taken an informal poll and received over 60 responses that desired the 
connection of Plantation Drive and an additional access be added through West Michigan 
Avenue. Mr. Koontz stated that there would be emergency access off of Windsong Drive 
and that potentially, depending on what the Fire Marshall would require, West Michigan 
Avenue. Mr. Koontz also stated that in the case of an emergency the residents would be 
able to use the emergency access as a point of egress and Windsong Drive, during 
construction, would also be used as a construction access. Once construction was 
complete it would be used for emergency vehicle access.  
 
Gerald Feeny, the President of the Mid-South POA Board of Directors, explained that 
originally the Board of Directors had concerns over traffic congestion, the circulation of 
construction vehicles, the type of housing that was proposed to be built, and the location 
of emergency access points. However, to date, their questions had been answered by the 
developer. He also expressed that he did not foresee any issues with the Mid-South POA 
regulating construction traffic coming through the main gate.  
 
Leena Sellers, who resides at 98 Plantation Drive, asked if the board would be willing to 
mandate that all construction vehicles be limited to the use of Windsong Drive as the 
construction access. Mr. Koontz stated that this would not be an issue in the future 
because the only access to the phases was through Windsong Drive. Heavy Construction 
vehicles would not be using the main gate. Andy Bleggi, member of the Planning Board, 
stated that control of construction vehicles should be left to the discretion of the Mid-
South POA and that the roads in Mid-South were private roads. Discussion ensued as to 
the authority that should regulate construction vehicles and it was recommended by the 
Planning Board that the construction vehicles follow the direction of the Mid-South POA 
in regards to their access and circulation. Joseph Sellers, also residing at 98 Plantation 
Drive, asked about the bridge on Palmer Drive and stated that the developers did not 
address what their plan was if the bridge was compromised. Mr. Sellers also stated that 
the TIA that had been submitted was not conducted during the Golf season when traffic 
would be at its highest levels. Mr. Koontz stated that the TIA conducted utilized 
historical data from NCDOT as well as a specific day chosen by the Traffic Engineer.  
 
Gary Podlogar, who resides at 10 Plantation Drive, stated that he had concerns about the 
developer clear cutting the existing tress and requested that the developer be held to the 
same standards that residents of Mid-South are held to when undergoing review by the 
Mid-South Architectural Review Board.  BJ Grieve, Planning Director for the Town of 
Southern Pines, explained that in the state of North Carolina there were specific 
limitations on regulation of architecture and should be a matter for the Mid-South POA.  
Meredith Jones, who did not identify her place of residence, asked what type of security 
features would secure the emergency access point. Mr. Koontz explained that they had 
not yet finalized but ensured that it would be secured and in compliance with the 
requirements of the Town Fire Marshall.

After hearing testimony form those wishing to speak the Planning Board closed the 
public hearing and proceeded with Board Discussion. The Board asked members of staff 
and Mr. Koontz questions concerning the future connection of Plantation Drive and about 
securing the Emergency Access, about the recommendations made by fish and wildlife to 
have the property surveyed. Mr. Koontz stated that they intended to have a survey done 
and that the connection of the Plantation Drive loop would be completed in Future 
phases. Mr. Koontz requested that a deviation be recommended by Planning Board and 
granted by Town Council, that the requirement for street trees and sidewalks be waived 
so that the proposed extensions of streets within the Mid-South development were 
consistent with the existing streets.  
 
After discussing the public’s testimony, Diane Westbrooke made a motion to adopt 
Attachment A of the staff report. The motion was seconded by Lem Dowdy. Ms. 
Westbrooke then read the conditions of approval that Planning Board wished to forward 
to Town Council and made a motion to recommend approval of CU-03-19. Ms. 
Westbrooke then made a motion to adopt attachment B of the Staff report, seconded by 
Mr. Dowdy. Ms. Westbrooke then made a motion to recommend approval of S-48-19 to 
the Town Council. The motion was seconded by Mr. Dowdy. All motions were carried 
unanimously.

iv. 
Zoning History: 
In 1988 the rezoning Z-15-87 was approved for 535 acres, originally called the 
Voit-Gilmore tract, now comprising the Mid-South tract. The rezoning amended 
the tract on the zoning map from RA, RS-2, and RSMH to RS-2CD for a residential 
subdivision with a golf course (see figure 1). Included in Z-15-87 was a master plan 
approving 647 dwelling units for a total gross density of 1.21 dwelling units per 
acre. The master plan included three types of residential uses: 384 Single-Family 
lots on 208.70 acres; 119 Cottages on 22.08 acres; and 144 Multi-Family Units on 
15.84 acres. Land approved for development with residential uses totaled 246.62 
acres. The golf course was approved on another 178.60 acres (133.5 acres of golf 
course and 45.1 acres of natural area adjoining the golf corridors). To date, 468 
dwelling units have gone through site plan review and have been platted.  
 
v. 
Existing Zoning:  
The site is currently zoned Residential Single Family-2 Conditional District (RS-
2CD). The standards for development within the RS-2CD can be found in the 
Conditional Rezoning Z-15-87. At the time of the rezoning, golf courses were a 
conditional use in the RS-2 district. The site is surrounded by a mix of residential 
and recreational districts. To the north is Residential Single Family-2 (RS-2). To 
the east are Facilities Resource and Recreation (FRR) as well as Residential Single 
Family-1 (RS-1). To the south is a Planned Development (PD) and to the west are 
RS-2, FRR, and General Business (GB).

B. Criteria for Review:  
i. Conditional Use Permit (UDO §2.21.7): 
A conditional Use is permitted only if the applicant demonstrates that: 
A. The proposed conditional use shall comply with all regulations of 
the applicable zoning district and any applicable supplemental use 
regulations; 
B. The proposed conditional use shall conform to the character of the 
neighborhood in which it is located and not injure the use and 
enjoyment of property in the immediate vicinity for the purposes 
already permitted; 
C. Adequate public facilities shall be provided as set forth herein; 
D. The proposed use shall not impede the orderly Development and 
improvement of surrounding property for uses permitted within the 
zoning district or substantially diminish or impair the property 
values within the neighborhood; 
E. The establishment, maintenance, or operation of the proposed use 
shall not be detrimental to or endanger the public health, safety, 
comfort or general welfare; and, 
F. The public interest and welfare supporting the proposed use shall 
be sufficient to outweigh individual interests that are adversely 
affected by the establishment of the proposed use. 
 
ii. Major Subdivision Preliminary Plat - UDO §2.20.5(G): 
CU-03-19 & S-48-19 Midsouth East End
June 2020 Town Council
Page 7 of 140
1. The application is consistent with the approved Sketch Plat, if 
applicable. 
2. The application is consistent with the Comprehensive Plan, as well as 
any other adopted plans for streets, alleys, parks, playgrounds, and 
public utility facilities;  
3. The proposed subdivision complies with the UDO and applicable state 
and federal regulations; 
4. The proposed subdivision, including its Lot sizes, density, access, and 
circulation, is compatible with the existing and/or permissible zoning 
and future land use of adjacent property; 
5. The proposed subdivision will not have detrimental impacts on the 
safety or viability of permitted uses on adjacent properties; and 
6. The proposed public facilities are adequate to serve the normal and 
emergency demands of the proposed Development, and to provide for 
the efficient and timely extension to serve future Development. 
 
C. Project Details and Compliance with the UDO:  
 
i. Description of Proposed Subdivision: 
The proposed subdivision is split into two phases. Phase One is a fifty-two-
lot subdivision for single-family residences that shows a disturbance area of 
4.76 acres. A requirement of subdivision in the UDO is that five percent of 
the total area of the development be dedicated towards usable open space in 
accordance with §4.9.1 Usable Open Space Required (A). There is no 
definable lot dedicated towards open space in this phase as would be 
required by §4.9.1 Usable Open Space Required (B)(5) [Usable open 
space] is part of an independent lot shown on the plan as being reserved 
for open space. However, other phases of this development may be used to 
meet the usable open space requirement as usable open space is calculated 
based on the total percentage provided throughout the development. Phase 
Two is a seven-lot subdivision for six single family residences and 
approximately 18,155 square feet of dedicated open space as the seventh 
lot. Phase Two proposes a disturbed area of 0.191 acres.   
 
ii. Existing and Proposed Public Infrastructure:  
a. Utilities:  
An existing 8” gravity sewer and a 6” water main run up to the 
subdivision phasing line for Phase One (see Figure 3). An extension of 
these mains will be required to service the 58 proposed residential lots 
for Phase One. The preliminary plat submitted for Phase One shows 
both these extensions within the proposed extension of Plantation Drive. 
The proposed extensions of public utilities will require the dedication of 
a right of way easement within the private street in order to service and 
maintain the lines. Phase Two currently has existing sewer and water 
running the length of the 60’ R/W for Plantation Drive and can be tapped 
for the proposed subdivision of 6 residential lots.  
CU-03-19 & S-48-19 Midsouth East End
June 2020 Town Council
Page 8 of 140
 
On May 11, 2020 the Town Engineer provided comments (comments 
included in agency referrals and as an attachment to this report) 
concerning the water line as proposed: “In accordance with Section 
4.15.8 Fire Hydrants (F) Water lines that serve hydrants shall be at least 
six (6) inch lines and unless no other practicable alternative is available, 
no such lines shall be dead-end lines. The purpose of the looping 
requirement is to ensure redundancy in providing drinking water to the 
Town’s customers, redundancy in firefighting capability, and provide a 
means for constant water turnover to prevent stagnation of the water in 
the lines.  The proposed layout shown in the Phase 1 Plat is not 
compliant with this requirement. The developer will need to coordinate 
with Public Works staff during the site plan review process to provide 
an acceptable means of looping to the dead-end line at the Windsong 
Drive intersection.”  
 
b. Stormwater 
The preliminary plat for Phase One shows existing storm drainage in a 
15’ easement to the north of the proposed subdivision and proposed 
drainage continuing along Plantation Drive to the south where there is a 
storm drainage pipe drawn with a rip-rap dissipater exceeding the 
southern phasing boundary line. The proposed drainage as drawn does 
not show how stormwater will be managed as there is no area designated 
on the preliminary plat for a storm water control measure. The 
preliminary plat for Phase Two shows existing storm drainage within a 
20’ easement that terminates at the rear of the proposed lots 84 and 85. 
The preliminary plat for Phase Two also does not have a designated area 
for storm water management. In an email response (see attachments) to 
an official communication for the completeness review of the 
submission, dated March 31, 2020, the applicant’s explanation of their 
stormwater management proposal for Phase Two was that the intention 
was to allow stormwater runoff to sheet flow across the lots and 
infiltrate the ground. The response also specifies that whatever does not 
infiltrate the ground will run into an existing pond at the rear of the lots.  
 
On May 11, 2020 the Town Engineer provided comments (comments 
included in agency referrals and as an attachment to this report) 
concerning the proposed storm water management: “In accordance with 
Section 4.14.3 Storm Water Management (3) The post-development 
runoff rate shall be equal to or less than the pre-development rate from 
the design storm or a ten (10) year storm event. The intent of this 
section, as described in the UDO, “All Developments shall be 
constructed and maintained so that adjacent properties are not 
unreasonably burdened with surface waters as a result of such 
Developments”. The developer will need to work with the Town 
Engineer during the site plan review process to provide acceptable 
CU-03-19 & S-48-19 Midsouth East End
June 2020 Town Council
Page 9 of 140
methods of stormwater control with supporting calculations for both 
phases of the project.” The Town Engineer also specified that his 
comments “(…) specifically address to items related to the Public 
Works review. This is not intended to imply that all other requirements 
have been met or that the developer was not planning to meet them as 
part of the engineering plan submittal, just that based on the information 
submitted, it is unclear how these two specific (comments relating to the 
water line extension and storm water) are going to be met. As with any 
site plan, the expectation is that all of the requirements described in the 
UDO will be met as part of the site design, and will be reviewed in more 
detail during the site plan review process.” 
 
c. Streets   
The preliminary plat for Phase One proposes an extension of Plantation 
Drive. The Powell Bill Map lists Plantation Drive as a private street (See 
figures 4 and 5). Plantation Drive as built up to the phasing line is a 
private street built to the town standard for a residential sub-collector in 
regards to the width of the travel lanes and its use of curbing. However, 
Plantation Drive as built is not built to the standards of the cross section 
for a 60’ R/W as shown in Appendix I: Street Cross Sections of the 
Town of Southern Pines Unified Development Ordinance in that no 
sidewalks have been built. The preliminary plat also shows a residential 
local street ending in a cul-de-sac that is currently proposed to be named 
Ambassador Court. Neither of the proposed streets specifies the 
proposed design standard or R/W to service the extension of public 
utilities. If the applicant is requesting to extend Plantation Drive and 
build Ambassador Court to the existing standards found for residential 
local and sub-collectors in the Mid-South development then it must be 
specifically stated in the application materials submitted. If a deviation 
from the design standards as specified in §4.11.10 Street Width, 
Sidewalk and Drainage Requirements in Subdivisions and Appendix I: 
Street Cross Sections of the UDO will be requested then it must 
specifically be granted by the Town Council in accordance with 
§4.11.10 (A) Street Width, Sidewalk and Drainage Requirements in 
Subdivisions: Street rights-of-way shall be designed and constructed in 
conformance with the provisions [herein] unless otherwise allowed for 
by the Town Council as part of a Conditional Use Permit or Planned 
Development Application. The preliminary plat for Phase Two shows 
an existing street for Plantation Drive, however the note on the 
preliminary plat calls Plantation Drive a 60’ Public R/W without the 
specification that Plantation Drive is a private street. The preliminary 
plat must specify that Plantation Drive is a private street in accordance 
with §4.11.14 (D) Private Streets in Subdivisions: The recorded plat of 
any subdivision shall clearly identify private streets.

d. Access  
The Traffic Impact Analysis (TIA) designates the access for ingress and 
egress to Phase One from Plantation Drive and designates Windsong 
Drive as an existing asphalt roadway to serve as the emergency access. 
On April 24, 2020 the Town Fire Marshall (comments included in 
agency referrals and as an attachment to this report) provided comments 
stating that Windsong Drive would not be considered an emergency 
access as it is listed unless improvements were made to the existing 
road. In its current state it is impassable to large trucks and additional 
access will be required. The suggestion was made that West Michigan 
could be another option and may be a better option due to it being 
shorter in length than Windsong Drive. Access to Phase Two is also 
provided by Plantation Drive and is an existing private street.  
 
On May 11, 2020 the Town Engineer provided comments (comments 
included in agency referrals and as an attachment to this report) 
concerning his review of the TIA: “The TIA recommends that actions 
be taken to maximize sight distance. In accordance with 4.12.5 (D) 
“Safety. Access points shall be designed to provide for adequate sight 
distance and appropriate facilities to accommodate acceleration and 
deceleration of site traffic pursuant to section 4.11.5.” Section 4.11.5 
references appendix C of the UDO, but Appendix C only provides the 
minimum sight distance required for a design speed of 30 MPH. Knoll 
road uses the Town standard speed limit of 35MPH which means the 
design speed of the road is 40MPH. The Engineering plans need to 
include improvements to the existing intersection of Knoll Road and 
Palmer to ensure that appropriate sight distance is provided for a design 
speed of 40MPH.”  
 
The applicant submitted images of the current intersection of Palmer 
Drive and Knoll Road, as well as a diagram of the intersection with 10’ 
by 70’ site distance triangles overlaid on an aerial image. However, staff 
is not able to identify any explanation of the images and diagram or 
statement(s) regarding that which the images and diagram are 
attempting to conclusively demonstrate. 
 
e. Buffers 
Both phases of the proposed subdivision are located on the eastern 
extremity of the development. The Voigt-Gilmore master plan shows a 
vegetated buffer running along the outer boundary of the Mid-South 
East End development. As such, both preliminary plats show a twenty-
five-foot undisturbed buffer between the proposed subdivided lots and 
the adjacent properties zoned RS-1 and FRR. The applicants should be 
aware now that this buffer shall be planted in accordance with the 
standards for buffers as set forth in UDO §4.3.4. Should any additional 
CU-03-19 & S-48-19 Midsouth East End
June 2020 Town Council
Page 14 of 140
plantings be required to address opacity standards for separation buffers, 
they will be addressed at site plan review.

iii. Compliance with the Comprehensive Land Use Plan (CLRP) and other 
Town adopted plans. 
a. Compliance with the CLRP 
The area proposed to be subdivided is designated as Residential/ Golf 
on the Future Land Use Map. The Residential/Golf designation applies 
to all “…areas that include public or private golf courses and residences. 
This category may accommodate a single family or attached dwellings 
at a variety of densities, recreational facilities in addition to the golf 
course, limited guest accommodations, and limited commercial services 
intended to serve residents of and visitors to the development.” The 
applicant has provided a narrative addressing a justification for 
compliance of the proposed subdivision with the CLRP. The applicant’s 
Conditional Use Permit justification narrative are attached to this memo.  
 
b. Compliance with Other Adopted Plans  
The Town of Southern Pines Comprehensive Recreation & Parks 
Master Plan addresses future access to recreation facilities and 
pedestrian and bicycle connectivity in the Town of Southern Pines. 
Although the Mill Creek Access Trail runs along the western extremity 
of the Mid-South-East End development, the currently proposed 
subdivision does not contain or is adjacent to any area that the trail runs 
through. Additionally, there are no recommendations for the Mid South-
East End development within the Comprehensive Recreation & Parks 
Master Plan.  
 
iv. General Staff Comments  
• The specific review process and criteria for a Conditional Use Permit 
and a Major Subdivision are found in §2.21.3 and § 2.20 of the UDO. 
The applicant has submitted narratives addressing compliance with the 
criteria, copies of which are attached to this report. 
 
• Pursuant to UDO §2.20.5(J)(4), an approved Preliminary Plat is vested 
for two (2) years, but may be vested longer if phased. The same section 
of the UDO as well as NCGS §160A-385.1(b), (c) and (d) allows a 
maximum vesting period of five (5) years for phased development 
plans. The applicant has addressed the proposed phasing in the 
application narrative submitted with the Conditional Use Permit. The 
applicant has requested that phases be allowed to develop in any order 
or concurrently.  
 
• Mid-South Phases One and Two will require site plan review by the 
Town of Southern Pines Technical Review Committee. Once site plans 
for each phase are complete, the required infrastructure must be 
installed per the approved plans or waived by the Town Manager 
pursuant to a Subdivision Improvement Agreement (UDO §2.20.7) or 
CU-03-19 & S-48-19 Midsouth East End
June 2020 Town Council
Page 17 of 140
addressed through a Development Agreement (UDO §2.20.8). Only 
upon completion or other satisfaction of the required infrastructure and 
approval of said infrastructure installation by the Town may the 
applicant apply for Major Subdivision Final Plat approval. 
 
A. Outside Agency Comments: 
 
A request for comments from agencies was emailed to representatives of 
the Town of Southern Pines Engineering, Streets, Utilities, Fire and 
Recreation & Parks Departments as well as representatives of the North 
Carolina Department of Transportation, U.S. Fish and Wildlife Service and 
the Regional Land Use Advisory Commission on April 30, 2020.  
 
o Comments were received from the Town of Southern Pines Town 
Engineer on May 11, 2020. The comments state as follows: 
 
1. In accordance with Section 4.15.8 Fire Hydrants (F) Water lines 
that serve hydrants shall be at least six (6) inch lines and unless 
no other practicable alternative is available, no such lines shall 
be dead-end lines. The purpose of the looping requirement is to 
ensure redundancy in providing drinking water to the Town’s 
customers, redundancy in firefighting capability, and provide a 
means for constant water turnover to prevent stagnation of the 
water in the lines.  The proposed layout shown in the Phase 1 
Plat is not compliant with this requirement. The developer will 
need to coordinate with Public Works staff during the site plan 
review process to provide an acceptable means of looping to the 
dead end line at the Windsong Drive intersection. 
 
2. In accordance with Section 4.14.3 Storm Water Management (3) 
The post-development runoff rate shall be equal to or less than 
the pre-development rate from the design storm or a ten (10) year 
storm event. The intent of this section, as described in the UDO, 
“All Developments shall be constructed and maintained so that 
adjacent properties are not unreasonably burdened with surface 
waters as a result of such Developments”. The developer will 
need to work with the Town Engineer during the site plan review 
process to provide acceptable methods of stormwater control 
with supporting calculations for both phases of the project. 
 
3. The above items 1 & 2 are specifically address to items related 
to the Public Works review. This is not intended to imply that 
all other requirements have been met or that the developer was 
not planning to meet them as part of the engineering plan 
submittal, just that based on the information submitted, it is 
unclear how these two specific are going to be met. As with any 
CU-03-19 & S-48-19 Midsouth East End
June 2020 Town Council
Page 18 of 140
site plan, the expectation is that all of the requirements described 
in the UDO will be met as part of the site design, and will be 
reviewed in more detail during the site plan review process. 
 
4. The TIA recommends that actions be taken to maximize sight 
distance. In accordance with 4.12.5 (D) “Safety. Access points 
shall be designed to provide for adequate sight distance and 
appropriate facilities to accommodate acceleration and 
deceleration of site traffic pursuant to section 4.11.5.” Section 
4.11.5 references appendix C of the UDO, but Appendix C only 
provides the minimum sight distance required for a design speed 
of 30 MPH. Knoll road uses the Town standard speed limit of 
35MPH which means the design speed of the road is 40MPH. 
The Engineering plans need to include improvements to the 
existing intersection of Knoll Road and Palmer to ensure that 
appropriate sight distance is provided for a design speed of 
40MPH.  
 
o Comments from the N.C. Sandhills Sub-Office of the U.S. Fish and 
Wildlife Service were received on May 7, 2020. The comments state 
as follows: 
 
“Due to the proximity of known active red‐cockaded 
woodpecker clusters, the project proponent should have this 
property surveyed by personnel experienced in management 
and monitoring of the species prior to the removal of any The 
results of this survey should be sent to the US Fish and Wildlife 
Service office located in Southern Pines, NC for review.” 
 
The applicant does not address “Endangered Species” in the 
Conditional Use Permit Justification Narrative that is attached to 
this memo.  
 
o Comments were received from the Town of Southern Pines Town 
Fire Marshall on April 24, 2020. The comments state as follows:  
 
“The only thing I would say is that Windsong Drive would not 
be considered an “Emergency Access” as they have it listed 
unless they plan to make improvements. In its current state it is 
impassable to large trucks and additional access will be 
required for this development. West Michigan could be another 
option and shorter.”  
 
o Any comments received after the publishing of this report will be 
forwarded to the Town Council at the public hearing as an exhibit.

To either approve or deny a Conditional Use Permit application, the Town Council 
shall make findings of fact and conclusions to the applicable standards. The Town 
Council shall first vote on whether the application is complete and whether the facts 
presented are relevant to the case.  The Town Council shall then vote on whether the 
application complies with the criteria as set forth in Section 2.21.7(A-F) Criteria for 
a Conditional Use Permit. The Town Council may choose one of the following motions 
or any alternative they wish:

ATTACHMENT “A” 
Draft Town Council Findings of Fact 
Conditional Use Permit Application CU-03-19 
 
Finding of Fact #1: 
 
The Town Council finds that the application is complete and that the facts submitted are relevant 
to the case because the request for Conditional Use Permit approval has met the specified submittal 
requirements as required in the Town of Southern Pines UDO Appendices and the evidence 
submitted was sworn testimony by qualified experts or provided through substantiated 
documentation. 
 
Finding of Fact #2: 
 
The Town Coucnil finds that the application complies with UDO §2.21.7 Criteria for a Conditional 
Use Permit, Criteria A-F, in that: 
 
A. The proposed conditional use shall comply with all regulations of the applicable 
zoning district and any applicable supplemental use regulations; 
The Town Council finds that application for CU-03-19 complies with the RS-2CD district 
and the development standards approved in the Voigt-Gilmore Master Plan. The applicant 
must adhere to the applicable development standards established in the UDO and no 
evidence of extraordinary circumstances which may allow the standards to be modified has 
been presented.    
 
B. The proposed conditional use shall conform to the character of the neighborhood in 
which it is located and not injure the use and enjoyment of property in the immediate 
vicinity for the purposes already permitted;  
The Town Council finds that the proposed development is in character with the existing 
development and the proposed 58 additional lots are below the 647 residential lots 
approved with Z-15-87. The proposed development is infill development that is compatible 
with the context of the surrounding neighborhood and does not exceed the existing 
approved uses or density.  
 
C. Adequate public facilities shall be provided as set forth herein;  
The Town Council finds that adequate facilities for sewer and water are in place based on 
information provided by the town and the applicant. The applicant has shown existing 
services for water and sewer within Phase Two and will need to extend utilities to serve 
the lots in Phase One. Although the Town Council finds that adequate ingress and egress 
has been addressed for both phases, the Town Council finds that the emergency access 
proposed in Phase One as the existing asphalt road Windsong Drive is not an adequate 
transportation facility for Emergency access. The proposed stormwater management will 
be addressed at TRC during final site plan review and must comply with the current 
development standards.   
  
CU-03-19 & S-48-19 Midsouth East End
June 2020 Town Council
Page 23 of 140
D. The proposed use shall not impede the orderly development and improvement of 
surrounding property for uses permitted within the zoning district or substantially 
diminish or impair the property values within the neighborhood; 
The Town Council finds that the proposed subdivision will likely not have detrimental 
impacts on the permitted uses of adjacent properties or impair property values because it 
is consistent with the original master plan and approved uses for the RS-2CD.  The Town 
Council also finds that the proposed development is located where public utilities currently 
exist and therefore does not impede the orderly development of surrounding property.  
   
E. The establishment, maintenance or operation for the proposed use shall not be 
detrimental to or endanger the public health, safety, comfort, or general welfare; and 
The Town Council finds that the proposed subdivision will not have detrimental impacts 
on the safety, comfort or general welfare because this subdivision will be required to adhere 
to all site development standards and building standards, including, but not limited to 
compliance with the building and fire code.  The applicants will be required to meet all 
conditions imposed as well as meet all regulatory measures set forth at final site plan 
review.   
 
F. The public interest and welfare supporting the proposed use shall be sufficient to 
outweigh individual interests that are adversely affected by the establishment of the 
proposed use; 
The Town Council finds that the proposed subdivision complies with applicable standards 
and regulations found within the Town of Southern Pines UDO that are based on the public 
interest and welfare.

Finding of Fact #1: 
 
The Town Council finds that the application is complete and that the facts submitted are relevant 
to the case because the request for Preliminary Plat approval has met the specified submittal 
requirements as required in the Town of Southern Pines UDO Appendices and the evidence 
submitted was sworn testimony by qualified experts or provided through substantiated

Finding of Fact #2: 
 
The Town Council finds that the application complies with UDO §2.20.5(G) Criteria for a 
Preliminary Plat, Criteria 1-6, in that: 
 
1. The application is consistent with the approved Sketch Plat, if applicable;  
The Town Council finds that the proposed Major Subdivision Preliminary Plat involves the 
subdivision of less than the entire contiguous land area of the parcel being subdivided, and 
therefore must have a Sketch plat. Per UDO §2.20.4(B) a Sketch Plat may be processed 
concurrently with a Preliminary Plat. As part of the CUP and Major Subdivision Preliminary 
Plat applications, the applicants have provided the materials required for review of a Sketch 
Plat per UDO Appendix A. The Town Council finds that per UDO §2.20.4(G), the proposed 
subdivision is consistent with the Town of Southern Pines Comprehensive Long Range Plan 
(CLRP), zoning map and the approved “Voigt Gilmore Master Plan.” The Phasing Schedule 
provided generally provides for the orderly development of lots and each phase may stand 
alone if development occurs in accordance with all applicable Town of Southern Pines design 
and construction standards. The Town Council also finds that the project is located in an 
appropriate area of Town for the reasons described in the Findings of Fact previously adopted 
with approval of the CUP.    
 
2. The application is consistent with the Comprehensive Plan, as well as any other adopted 
plans for streets, alleys, parks, playgrounds, and public utility facilities;  
The Town Council finds that the proposed Preliminary Plat is generally consistent with the 
standards set forth in the CLRP because different densities of residential development are 
proposed in a manner that is consistent with the RS2-CD. Streets, lot density, and open spaces 
are planned as part of the approved Voigt-Gilmore Master Plan but public water utilities will 
need to be designed with looped systems and approved following the Town’s Site Plan review 
process (UDO §2.48). Conceptual stormwater management plans have been provided for one 
out of the two proposed phases, but proper stormwater management facilities will be required 
and reviewed following the Town’s Site Plan review process (UDO §2.48).  
 
3. The proposed subdivision complies with the UDO and applicable state and federal 
regulations;  
CU-03-19 & S-48-19 Midsouth East End
June 2020 Town Council
Page 25 of 140
The proposed subdivision is part of an existing residential development. The Town Council 
recognizes that development standards at the time of the rezoning and phased subdivision of 
the Mid-South East-End tract have changed and therefore the proposed subdivision has been 
reviewed based on the criteria established in the most recent adopted Unified Development 
Ordinance. The project will not be granted Site Plan approval per UDO §2.48 without 
necessary approvals from applicable state and federal agencies. The burden of demonstrating 
compliance with applicable state and federal regulations rests with the applicant per UDO 
§2.5.6.  
  
4. The proposed subdivision, including its Lot sizes, density, access, and circulation, is 
compatible with the existing and / or permissible zoning and future land use of adjacent 
property; 
The proposed subdivision is zoned Residential Single Family-2 Conditional District, a mixed-
use zoning classification with a variety of approved residential product types and densities. 
The Town Council finds that the proposed subdivision is compatible and consistent with this 
zoning classification with regard to the dimensional and density regulations.  The proposed 
subdivision is also compatible with the zoning and future land uses of adjacent property.  The 
surrounding properties are developed with residential land uses with a similar diversity of 
densities and open spaces. The Town Council finds that the current design for emergency 
access in Phase One is not adequate access for internal vehicular circulation of emergency 
services and waste removal vehicles.  Access to the subdivision was assessed in the Traffic 
Impact Analysis (TIA) that were submitted by the applicant. The TIA was reviewed by both 
the North Carolina Department of Transportation (NCDOT), the Town of Southern Pines 
Town Engineer, and the Town of Southern Pines Fire Marshall and recommendations were 
made by the Town Engineer and the Town Fire Marshall.   
 
5. The proposed subdivision will not have detrimental impacts on the safety or viability of 
permitted uses on adjacent properties; and 
The Town Council finds that the proposed subdivision will not have detrimental impacts on 
the safety or viability of permitted uses on adjacent properties because the land use is 
compatible with existing and allowable uses on adjacent properties per the zoning map and the 
development is consistent with the CLRP. During the process of reviewing engineering plans 
for Midsouth East End, per UDO §2.20.6 and UDO §2.48, the site distance requirements for 
the intersection of Palmer Drive and Knoll Road will be assessed in detail and physical 
improvements to the intersection may be required prior to approval of a Final Plat.    
 
6. The proposed public facilities are adequate to serve the normal and emergency demands 
of the proposed development, and to provide for the efficient and timely extension to 
serve future development; 
The Town Council finds that public water and sewer utilities are available and can be extended 
to serve the project. Looped public water lines and adequate stormwater facilities will be 
verified prior to approval of site plans for any of the individual phases of the proposed 
subdivision. Site access is provided via Plantation Drive for both phases. An improved 
emergency access for Windsong Drive will be required for emergency access prior to site plan 
approval.

MIDSOUTH PROPERTY 
CONDITIONAL USE PERMIT NARRATIVE 
 
The development of the property described as the Midsouth Property in the submitted exhibits is an 
approved mixed-residential subdivision, rezoned in 1988, located on the south side of Midland Road 
between Midland Road and Morganton Road. The 535.58-acre property is zoned RS-2 CD, which is 
primarily a single-family residential zoning district with conditional approval for a golf course; the 
current requests involve 62.5 acres of the 535.5 acre tract. The RS-2 base zoning allows low-density 
residential uses as stated in Section 3.5.4 of the Town of Southern Pines Unified Development 
Ordinance.   
 
This conditional use permit application proposes lots in two areas of the approved Conditional Use 
Permit: 
• 
Phase 1: Plat fifty-two (52) lots and open space lot along the extension of Plantation Drive, south 
of Claret Court. Residential lot sizes will vary as permitted in the previously approved conditional 
zoning. 
• 
Phase 2: Plat six (6) single-family lots and 18,155 square feet of open space on a parcel located 
east of the intersection of Plantation Drive with Hadley Court; request includes rerouting of a 
storm drainage easement. Residential lot sizes will vary as permitted in the previously approved 
conditional zoning. 
 
In September of 1988, a conditional use permit was approved which permitted a total of 647 dwelling 
units of mixed residential types. To date, 468 residential dwellings or lots have been approved through 
previous CUPs.  
 
This Conditional Use Permit request plats 58 new single-family lots, in addition to open space. This 
requires a Conditional Use Permit. With the addition of the 58 lots, the total approved/platted lots will 
increase to 526, leaving the ability to develop an additional 121 residential units with a later CUP 
application. The applicant requests that phases can be developed in any order, or concurrently.  
 
The development will meet the approved development standards for the RS-2 CD district and any other 
Town of Southern Pines UDO requirements. The approved open space amount of 128.3 acres will still be 
maintained with as permitted in the original conditional district.  
 
Adequate water and sewer service have been provided by the Town of Southern Pines to service this 
development. Utilities are currently along the streets; all utilities on the site will be located 
underground.    
 
The descriptions and conditions described above will apply to the entire project as indicated in the 
Conditional Use Permit application and preliminary plat.

EXHIBIT A 
 
Midsouth Property 
Conditional Use Permit Justification  
 
Below are listed the six (6) criteria required to approve a Conditional Use Permit application as described in Section 
2.21.7 of the Town of Southern Pines UDO.  Following the individual criteria is an explanation, indicated in red, 
describing how the project demonstrates compliance with each of these criteria. 
A Conditional Use is permitted only if the Applicant demonstrates that:  
 
(A) The proposed conditional use shall comply with all regulations of the applicable zoning district and any 
applicable supplemental use regulations;  
The proposed development will comply with all regulations of the RS-2 CD zoning district and any 
applicable supplemental use regulations. All single-family lots created will meet the standards specified in 
the RS-2 CD district and provide appropriate setbacks for the RS-2 CD zoning district. Access will meet the 
Town’s requirements. 
 
(B) The proposed conditional use shall conform to the character of the neighborhood in which it is located 
and not injure the use and enjoyment of property in the immediate vicinity for the purposes already 
permitted;  
The conditional use meets the standards of the zoning district and is in character with the surrounding 
properties. The proposed single-family detached units are still below the 647 total residential units 
permitted under the property’s zoning. 
 
(C) Adequate public facilities shall be provided as set forth herein;  
 
Public water and sewer utilities are readily available for the project, any cost of which will be borne by the 
 
developer. Lots will have adequate access to accommodate emergency and waste removal vehicles. 
 
(D) The proposed use shall not impede the orderly Development and improvement of surrounding property 
for uses permitted within the zoning district or substantially diminish or impair the property values within 
the neighborhood;  
This project will not impede the development of surrounding properties as it is in conformance with the 
surrounding development and zoning classifications as described in Item B of this exhibit. 
 
(E) The establishment, maintenance, or operation of the proposed use shall not be detrimental to or 
endanger the public health, safety, comfort or general welfare; and 
This residential neighborhood will continue the existing development pattern in the neighborhood and 
will conform to all development standards of the UDO and engineering requirements of the Town. As a 
result, the use will not be detrimental to or endanger the public health, safety, comfort or general welfare 
of the surrounding neighborhood. 
 
(F) The public interest and welfare supporting the proposed use shall be sufficient to outweigh individual 
interests that are adversely affected by the establishment of the proposed use. 
The conditional use is in compliance with the established development pattern and is in context with the 
underlying zoning district.  This project is also consistent with the goals and objectives of the 
Comprehensive Long Range Plan (CLRP) and establishes a development pattern that is in context with the 
surrounding neighborhood and the projects in this area of Southern Pines.  
 
The development pattern also meets the land use goals defined by the CLRP by adding development 
where public utilities are available and developing infill locations near downtown Southern Pines.

RE: Mid South – East End, Southern Pines, NC – Traffic Impact Analysis 
 
Dear Mr. Levy, 
Kimley-Horn has performed a Traffic Impact Analysis (TIA) for the proposed 58 additional single family 
dwelling units within the Mid South development in Southern Pines, NC. The homes will be accessed 
via the existing street network and the extension of  Plantation Drive. The development has a projected 
build-out year of 2025. 
This report presents trip generation, distribution, traffic analyses, and recommendations for 
transportation improvements required to meet anticipated traffic demands in conjunction with the 
proposed development in the projected (2025) build-out year and the projected (2030) ten-year horizon 
condition per the Town’s UDO. The site location is shown on Figure 1, and Figures 2A and 2B show 
the preliminary site plans. The existing roadway laneage at the study intersections is shown on Figure 
3. 
Existing and Background Traffic 
AM and PM peak hour turning movement counts performed on February 4, 2020 at the following 
intersections: 
 
S Knoll Road at Palmer Drive 
 
S Knoll Road at Felton Capel Lane at Voit Gilmore Lane (roundabout) 
 
Felton Capel Lane at Plantation Drive 
Based on historic daily traffic volumes in the area, an annual growth factor of 1% was applied to existing 
volumes for the 2025 and 2030 study year scenarios.  
 
Peak hour existing and background traffic volumes for the year 2025, which include historic growth 
traffic are shown on Figures 4 and 5. For the study year 2030, 2025 background and 2030 background 
traffic volumes are shown on Figures 6 and 7.  
Trip Generation 
The trip generation potential of the development was determined using the traffic generation rates 
published in the ITE Trip Generation Handbook (Institute of Transportation Engineers, Tenth Edition, 
2017). Table 1 summarizes the estimated traffic generation potential for the site.

Table 1 shows that the site has the potential to generate 630 new trips on a typical weekday with 46 
new trips during the AM peak hour and 60 new trips in the PM peak hour.  
It should be noted that the traffic counts performed at the Mid South driveways indicate that the homes 
in Mid South currently generate approximately 26% fewer AM peak hour trips and 48% fewer PM peak 
hour trips than ITE trip generation rates would suggest. Therefore, the analysis presented herein is 
expected to be very conservative.

distribution below. The directional distribution and assignment were based on existing Mid South travel 
patterns.

peak hour site and build-out traffic volumes at the study, respectively.

are summarized in Table 2.

Analysis indicates that all study intersections are expected to operate at an acceptable LOS in the 
projected 2025 and 2030 build-out traffic conditions. 
Crash Data Analysis 
Crash data reports were obtained from NCDOT for the study intersection of S Knoll Road at Palmer 
Drive for the period from January 2015 through December 2019. There were 7 reported crashes 
identified at or in the vicinity of this intersection in the provided data period. Three crashes were reported 
as Class C crashes and four as property-damage only crashes, resulting in a calculated crash severity 
index of 4.17. There were no significant crash patterns identified based on the provided data, and there 
is no reason to expect that traffic associated with this development will increase crash rates at this 
intersection. All provided crash data reports are included in the Appendix. 
Conclusions 
We understand that Mid South residents have requested that a traffic signal be installed at the 
intersection of S Knoll Road at Palmer Drive. However, it is unlikely that a traffic signal is or will be 
warranted at this location based on the existing and projected traffic volumes or the results of the crash 
data analysis. Efforts should be made to maximize sight distance for vehicles exiting Mid South; 
however, as the analysis indicates no capacity or queueing issues at any of the of the study 
intersections, no roadway improvements are recommended to be performed as part of this project to 
accommodate site traffic volumes. 
Should you have any questions or comments, please do not hesitate to contact me at (919) 653-2948 
or travis.fluitt@kimley-horn.com. 
Sincerely, 
 
Travis Fluitt, P.E. 
Senior Project Manager

Site Level of Service (LOS) Method: Delay & v/c (HCM 6). Site LOS Method is specified in the Parameter Settings dialog (Site tab).
Roundabout LOS Method: Same as Sign Control.
Vehicle movement LOS values are based on average delay and v/c ratio (degree of saturation) per movement.
LOS F will result if v/c > 1 irrespective of movement delay value (does not apply for approaches and intersection).
Intersection and Approach LOS values are based on average delay for all movements (v/c not used as specified in HCM 6).
Roundabout Capacity Model: US HCM 6.
HCM Delay Formula option is used. Control Delay does not include Geometric Delay since Exclude Geometric Delay option applies.
Gap-Acceptance Capacity: Traditional M1.
HV (%) values are calculated for All Movement Classes of All Heavy Vehicle Model Designation.

Site Level of Service (LOS) Method: Delay & v/c (HCM 6). Site LOS Method is specified in the Parameter Settings dialog (Site tab).
Roundabout LOS Method: Same as Sign Control.
Vehicle movement LOS values are based on average delay and v/c ratio (degree of saturation) per movement.
LOS F will result if v/c > 1 irrespective of movement delay value (does not apply for approaches and intersection).
Intersection and Approach LOS values are based on average delay for all movements (v/c not used as specified in HCM 6).
Roundabout Capacity Model: US HCM 6.
HCM Delay Formula option is used. Control Delay does not include Geometric Delay since Exclude Geometric Delay option applies.
Gap-Acceptance Capacity: Traditional M1.
HV (%) values are calculated for All Movement Classes of All Heavy Vehicle Model Designation.

Site Level of Service (LOS) Method: Delay & v/c (HCM 6). Site LOS Method is specified in the Parameter Settings dialog (Site tab).
Roundabout LOS Method: Same as Sign Control.
Vehicle movement LOS values are based on average delay and v/c ratio (degree of saturation) per movement.
LOS F will result if v/c > 1 irrespective of movement delay value (does not apply for approaches and intersection).
Intersection and Approach LOS values are based on average delay for all movements (v/c not used as specified in HCM 6).
Roundabout Capacity Model: US HCM 6.
HCM Delay Formula option is used. Control Delay does not include Geometric Delay since Exclude Geometric Delay option applies.
Gap-Acceptance Capacity: Traditional M1.
HV (%) values are calculated for All Movement Classes of All Heavy Vehicle Model Designation.

Site Level of Service (LOS) Method: Delay & v/c (HCM 6). Site LOS Method is specified in the Parameter Settings dialog (Site tab).
Roundabout LOS Method: Same as Sign Control.
Vehicle movement LOS values are based on average delay and v/c ratio (degree of saturation) per movement.
LOS F will result if v/c > 1 irrespective of movement delay value (does not apply for approaches and intersection).
Intersection and Approach LOS values are based on average delay for all movements (v/c not used as specified in HCM 6).
Roundabout Capacity Model: US HCM 6.
HCM Delay Formula option is used. Control Delay does not include Geometric Delay since Exclude Geometric Delay option applies.
Gap-Acceptance Capacity: Traditional M1.
HV (%) values are calculated for All Movement Classes of All Heavy Vehicle Model Designation.

Site Level of Service (LOS) Method: Delay & v/c (HCM 6). Site LOS Method is specified in the Parameter Settings dialog (Site tab).
Roundabout LOS Method: Same as Sign Control.
Vehicle movement LOS values are based on average delay and v/c ratio (degree of saturation) per movement.
LOS F will result if v/c > 1 irrespective of movement delay value (does not apply for approaches and intersection).
Intersection and Approach LOS values are based on average delay for all movements (v/c not used as specified in HCM 6).
Roundabout Capacity Model: US HCM 6.
HCM Delay Formula option is used. Control Delay does not include Geometric Delay since Exclude Geometric Delay option applies.
Gap-Acceptance Capacity: Traditional M1.
HV (%) values are calculated for All Movement Classes of All Heavy Vehicle Model Designation.

Site Level of Service (LOS) Method: Delay & v/c (HCM 6). Site LOS Method is specified in the Parameter Settings dialog (Site tab).
Roundabout LOS Method: Same as Sign Control.
Vehicle movement LOS values are based on average delay and v/c ratio (degree of saturation) per movement.
LOS F will result if v/c > 1 irrespective of movement delay value (does not apply for approaches and intersection).
Intersection and Approach LOS values are based on average delay for all movements (v/c not used as specified in HCM 6).
Roundabout Capacity Model: US HCM 6.
HCM Delay Formula option is used. Control Delay does not include Geometric Delay since Exclude Geometric Delay option applies.
Gap-Acceptance Capacity: Traditional M1.
HV (%) values are calculated for All Movement Classes of All Heavy Vehicle Model Designation.

Site Level of Service (LOS) Method: Delay & v/c (HCM 6). Site LOS Method is specified in the Parameter Settings dialog (Site tab).
Roundabout LOS Method: Same as Sign Control.
Vehicle movement LOS values are based on average delay and v/c ratio (degree of saturation) per movement.
LOS F will result if v/c > 1 irrespective of movement delay value (does not apply for approaches and intersection).
Intersection and Approach LOS values are based on average delay for all movements (v/c not used as specified in HCM 6).
Roundabout Capacity Model: US HCM 6.
HCM Delay Formula option is used. Control Delay does not include Geometric Delay since Exclude Geometric Delay option applies.
Gap-Acceptance Capacity: Traditional M1.
HV (%) values are calculated for All Movement Classes of All Heavy Vehicle Model Designation.

Site Level of Service (LOS) Method: Delay & v/c (HCM 6). Site LOS Method is specified in the Parameter Settings dialog (Site tab).
Roundabout LOS Method: Same as Sign Control.
Vehicle movement LOS values are based on average delay and v/c ratio (degree of saturation) per movement.
LOS F will result if v/c > 1 irrespective of movement delay value (does not apply for approaches and intersection).
Intersection and Approach LOS values are based on average delay for all movements (v/c not used as specified in HCM 6).
Roundabout Capacity Model: US HCM 6.
HCM Delay Formula option is used. Control Delay does not include Geometric Delay since Exclude Geometric Delay option applies.
Gap-Acceptance Capacity: Traditional M1.
HV (%) values are calculated for All Movement Classes of All Heavy Vehicle Model Designation.

Monday, May 11, 2020 9:47 AM

BJ Grieve; Lauren Long; Cindy Williams
Subject:
FW: CU-03-19 Mid South Conditional Use Permit
Attachments:
CU-03-19 PB PHN - Agency Referrals.pdf
Good morning to all of the wonderful planning staff involved in this project. Below are Public Works Comments on the 
submitted CUP. 
1. In accordance with Section 4.15.8 Fire Hydrants (F) Water lines that serve hydrants shall be at least six (6) inch 
lines and unless no other practicable alternative is available, no such lines shall be dead‐end lines. The purpose 
of the looping requirement is to ensure redundancy in providing drinking water to the Town’s customers, 
redundancy in firefighting capability, and provide a means for constant water turnover to prevent stagnation of 
the water in the lines.  The proposed layout shown in the Phase 1 Plat is not compliant with this requirement. 
The developer will need to coordinate with Public Works staff during the site plan review process to provide an 
acceptable means of looping to the dead end line at the Windsong Drive intersection. 
2. In accordance with Section 4.14.3 Storm Water Management (3) The post‐development runoff rate shall be 
equal to or less than the pre‐development rate from the design storm or a ten (10) year storm event. The intent 
of this section, as described in the UDO, “All Developments shall be constructed and maintained so that adjacent 
properties are not unreasonably burdened with surface waters as a result of such Developments”. The 
developer will need to work with the Town Engineer during the site plan review process to provide acceptable 
methods of stormwater control with supporting calculations for both phases of the project. 
3. The above items 1 & 2 are specifically address to items related to the Public Works review. This is not intended 
to imply that all other requirements have been met or that the developer was not planning to meet them as part 
of the engineering plan submittal, just that based on the information submitted, it is unclear how these two 
specific are going to be met. As with any site plan, the expectation is that all of the requirements described in 
the UDO will be met as part of the site design, and will be reviewed in more detail during the site plan review 
process. 
4. The TIA recommends that actions be taken to maximize sight distance. In accordance with 4.12.5 (D) “Safety. 
Access points shall be designed to provide for adequate sight distance and appropriate facilities to 
accommodate acceleration and deceleration of site traffic pursuant to section 4.11.5.” Section 4.11.5 references 
appendix C of the UDO, but Appendix C only provides the minimum sight distance required for a design speed of 
30 MPH. Knoll road uses the Town standard speed limit of 35MPH which means the design speed of the road is 
40MPH. The Engineering plans need to include improvements to the existing intersection of Knoll Road and 
Palmer to ensure that appropriate sight distance is provided for a design speed of 40MPH.  
 
 
Let me know if you have any questions. 
 
Thanks 
 
James Michel, PE, MBA

Due to the proximity of known active red‐cockaded woodpecker clusters, the project proponent should have this 
property surveyed by personnel experienced in management and monitoring of the species prior to the removal of any 
mature pine trees. Further guidance can be found at  www.fws.gov/ncsandhills/pine_tree_removal.html .  The results of 
this survey should be sent to the US Fish and Wildlife Service office located in Southern Pines, NC for review.

Agenda Item 
To: 
Reagan Parsons, Town Manager

BJ Grieve, Planning Director 
From: 
Suzy Russell, Planner II 
Subject: 
Z-02-20:  Request to rezone a 13.36 acre parcel and 22.07
acre  parcel located at 200 Meyer Farm Drive from RS-3
(Residential Single-Family) to RM-2 (Residential Mixed-
Housing); Applicant: Mr. Earl Ellis of Colony 9, LLC
Date: 
June 9, 2020 
I.
SUMMARY OF APPLICATION REQUEST:
Mr. Earl Ellis of Colony 9, LLC requests to rezone a 13.36 acre parcel and 22.07 acre
parcel located within Forest Creek at 200 Meyer Farm Drive from RS-3 (Residential
Single-Family) to RM-2 (Residential Mixed-Housing); The subject property is identified
as PIN: 857300393172 (PARID: 00037691).  Per the Moore County tax records, the
property owner is listed as Colony 9, LLC.
II.
PLANNING BOARD ACTION:
At the May 21, 2020 Regular Meeting of the Planning Board, the Planning Board held a
legislative hearing and heard from staff as well as those in attendance regarding application
Z-02-20. Planning staff entered the staff report Z-02-20 into the record as Exhibit A and
presented a review of the Zoning Map Amendment application. Planning staff discussed
consistency with the Comprehensive Long Range Plan (CLRP).
Following staff’s presentation, the applicant’s authorized agent Robert Koontz with 
KoontzJones Design presented a PowerPoint presentation (Exhibit B) of the proposed 
Zoning Map Amendment.  Mr. Koontz answered a variety of questions from the Public 
concerning POA guidelines for Architectural Review, expected expansion on the west side 
of Meyer Farm Drive, and if the general public were informed about this.  There was no 
testimony provided by members of the public.  
After hearing staff and the applicant speak, the Chairman closed the public comment 
portion of the hearing and proceeded with Board Discussion. Ms. Diane Westbrook made 
a motion to recommend approval of the Zoning Amendment Z-02-20. The motion was 
seconded by Mr. Lemuel Dowdy. The motion passed unanimously (Cooper Carter was 
absent) (6-0). The plan consistency statement adopted by the Planning Board may be found 
attached to this staff report. 
Z-02-20 Forest Creek
June 2020 Town Council
Page 1 of 43
III. 
PROJECT INFORMATION: 
 
A. Physical Address: 
200 Meyer Farm Drive 
Pinehurst, NC 28374 
 
B. Owner / Applicant: 
Colony 9, LLC 
Mr. Earl Ellis 
19 Cumberland Drive 
Pinehurst, NC 28374 
 
C. Authorized Agent: 
Mr. Bob Koontz 
Koontz Jones Design, PLLC 
150 S Page Street 
Southern Pines, NC 28387 
 
D. Current Zoning: 
The area requested to be rezoned is presently zoned RS-3 Residential Single-Family 
(see Figure 1 below). The RS-3 zoning district has the following purpose (UDO 
§3.5.5): 
 
The RS-3 district is designed to allow primarily very low density single-family 
residential land uses. The regulations of this district are intended to:  
1) Preserve existing Single-Family residential neighborhoods that have 
developed at a low-density; and  
2) Encourage new residential Development that is compatible with that in the 
existing neighborhoods. 
 
Land uses that are allowed by-right in the RS-3 zoning district are much lower in 
intensity of dwelling units than RM-2 zoning districts.  Multi-Family condominium 
land use, LBCS Code 1153 is allowed in RM-2 but is not allowed in RS-3.   LBCS 
Code 1153 is described as three or more dwelling units that are individually owned 
and common elements owned by the unit owners as tenants in-common.  RM-2 
zoning districts establish increases in intensity of dwelling units.  Private golf 
course land use is allowed in RS-3 zoning districts but are not allowed in RM-2 
zoning districts.    
 
E. Current Comprehensive Long-Range Plan Designation: 
 
The subject property is identified as Residential/Golf in the Future Land Use Plan 
2016 (see Figure 6).  Per the CLRP, the Residential/Golf designation applies to 
areas that include public or private golf courses and residences.  This category may 
accommodate single family or attached dwellings at a variety of densities, 
recreational facilities in addition to the golf course, limited guest accommodations, 
Z-02-20 Forest Creek
June 2020 Town Council
Page 2 of 43
and limited commercial services intended to serve residents of and visitors to the 
development.   
 
The future land use map is a graphic expression of the CLRP’s land-use policy.  
Provided to guide decisions on land use the map reflects both current uses- 
categorized more generally than with the Town’s zoning map – as well as uses the 
Town sees as conducive to the community’s long-range goals.  As opportunity and 
interest emerge for changes in land use and development regulation, the map should 
be referenced to ensure those changes meet overall planning goals.  In contrast to 
the Town’s parcel-specific zoning map adopted as part of the Town’s Unified 
Development Ordinance, the future land use map is presented with soft-edged use 
boundaries, which are intended to identify future land use designations but at the 
same time reflect the fact that as policy, specific boundaries are less critical than 
the map’s overall intent, including development type, intensities and their relative 
arrangement.   
 
The proposed amendment appears to be generally consistent with both the CLRP 
Future Land Use Map as well as with many Goals and Policies in the CLRP.  
Specifically Policy 12, stating that new housing choices foster the provision of a 
mix of housing that meets the financial and physical needs of existing and future 
residents by encouraging development of a variety of housing types in new 
residential areas and promoting compatible infill in existing neighborhoods.

F. Proposed Zoning: 
The applicant is requesting to zone the subject property RM-2 Residential Mixed-
Housing. The RM-2 zoning district has the following purpose (UDO §3.5.7): 
 
“The RM-2 district is established as a district in which to allow primarily Single-
Family and Multi-Family Residences at a moderate-density (approximately 5-7 
Dwelling Units per acre) in areas served by adequate public water and sewer 
systems. The regulations of this district are intended to:  
(1) Encourage Single-Family and Multi-Family Residences; and  
(2) Encourage new residential Development that is compatible with that in the 
existing neighborhoods. 
 
IV. 
STAFF REVIEW 
 
A. Review Process: 
Amendments to the Town of Southern Pines Official Zoning Map are reviewed 
pursuant to UDO §2.17.  
 
B. Application Review Dates:

• Application Complete: April 20, 2020

C. Criteria For Review: 
When reviewing an application for zoning, the hearing bodies shall consider and be 
guided by the following criteria, as set forth in UDO §2.17.9: 
1. Consistency. Rezoning shall be consistent with the adopted Comprehensive 
Plan 
2. Adverse Impacts on Neighboring Lands. The Hearing Body shall consider 
the nature and degree of an adverse impact upon neighboring lands. Lots 
shall not be rezoned in a way that is substantially inconsistent with the uses 
of the surrounding area, whether more or less restrictive. The Town finds 
and determines that vast acreages of single-use zoning produces uniformity 
with adverse consequences, such as traffic congestion, air pollution, and 
Z-02-20 Forest Creek
June 2020 Town Council
Page 6 of 43
social alienation. Accordingly, rezoning may promote mixed uses subject to 
a high degree of design control.  
3. Suitability as Presently Zoned. The Hearing Body shall consider the 
suitability or unsuitability of the Tract for its use as presently zoned. This 
factor, like the others, should be weighed in relation to the other standards, 
and instances can exist in which the land may be rezoned to meet public 
need, to reflect substantially changed conditions in the neighborhood, or to 
effectuate important goals, objectives and policies of the Comprehensive 
Plan or UDO.  
4. Health, Safety, and Welfare. The amending ordinance must bear a 
substantial relationship to the public health, safety or general welfare, or 
protect and preserve historical and cultural places and areas. The rezoning 
may be justified, however, if a substantial public need or purpose exists, 
even if the private owner of the Tract will also benefit.  
5. Public Policy. Certain public policies in favor of the rezoning may be 
considered. Examples include a need for affordable housing, economic 
Development, mixed-use Development, or sustainable environmental 
features, which are consistent with neighborhood, area, or specific plans.  
6. Size of Tract. The Hearing Body shall consider the size, shape, and 
characteristics of the Tract in relation to the affected neighboring lands. 
Amendatory ordinances shall not rezone a single Lot when there have been 
no intervening changes or other saving characteristics. Proof that a small 
tract is unsuitable for use as zoned, or that there have been substantial 
changes in the immediate area, may justify ordinance rezoning.  
7. Other Factors. The Hearing Body may consider any other factors relevant 
to a rezoning application under state law. 
8. Applicant Representations. Except for rezoning requests submitted in 
accordance with the provisions herein for conditional use district 
rezonings, the Hearing Body shall not consider any representations made 
by the petitioner that, if the change is granted, the rezoned property will be 
used for only one of the possible range of uses permitted in the requested 
classification. Rather, the Hearing Body shall consider whether the entire 
range of permitted uses in the requested classification is more appropriate 
than the range of uses in the existing classification.

VI. 
TOWN COUNCIL ACTION: 
 
The Town Council shall hold a public hearing. After closing the public hearing, the 
Town Council shall consider the information gathered at the public hearing in light 
of the eight (8) criteria for zoning map amendments. The Council may choose to adopt 
findings of fact and conclusions based on the eight (8) criteria for zoning map 
amendments, but an adoption of findings and conclusions is not required.  
 
Afterwards, the Town Council shall vote on whether to approve or deny the proposed 
zoning amendment. As part of any approval or denial, in accordance with North 
Carolina law, the Town Council shall adopt a statement regarding consistency of the 
proposed amendment with the adopted Comprehensive Long Range Plan. The Town 
Council may make the following motion, or any alternative they wish: 
 
I move that after considering the criteria for a zoning map amendment found in UDO 
§2.17.9, the Town Council finds that: 
 
1. 
The requested Zoning Map Amendment is consistent with the 
Comprehensive Long Range Plan and the Town Council adopts the 
Resolution that is included as Attachment “A” in the staff memorandum for 
Z-02-20;  
 
2. 
The requested Zoning Map Amendment is consistent with the 
Comprehensive Long Range Plan and the Town Council adopts the 
Resolution that is included as Attachment “A” in the staff memorandum for 
Z-02-20 with the following edits or comments to Attachment “A”… 
 
3. 
The requested Zoning Map Amendment is not consistent with the 
Comprehensive Long Range Plan and the Town Council adopts the 
Resolution that is included as Attachment “A” in the staff memorandum for 
Z-02-20 with the following edits or comments to Attachment “A”… 
 
And, therefore, I move to:  
 
1. 
Approve Z-02-20;  
 
2. 
Approve Z-02-20 with the following conditions;  
 
3. 
Deny Z-02-20; 
 
4. 
(Take other action…)

REVIEW AND APPROVAL: 
1. Staff review:  Planning staff will review the application and notify the applicant if additional 
materials are needed.  
2. Public hearings:  The applicant is expected to attend a public hearing on the application before the 
Planning Board followed by a public hearing before the Town Council the following month.  (Please 
refer to the Application Processing Timeline to determine the hearing dates.)  The Planning Board 
will recommend approval, conditional approval or denial to the Town Council.  The Town Council 
will consider that recommendation, as well as evidence and testimony presented, and approve, 
conditionally approve or deny the rezoning request. 
3. Approval: The approval of an amendment to the UDO text or Zoning Map does not authorize the 
use, occupancy, or development of property until the applicant receives necessary development 
approvals, such as subdivision, site plan and building permits.  (UDO §2.17.12)
