UDO §2.17.9. Criteria for Zoning Map Amendments 
In its review of an application for a zoning map amendment, the Hearing Bodies shall consider the 
following criteria.  No single factor is controlling; instead each must be weighed in relation to the other 
standards. 
(A) Consistency.  Rezoning shall be consistent with the adopted Comprehensive Plan.
(B) Adverse Impacts on Neighboring Lands.  The Hearing Body shall consider the nature and degree of
an adverse impact upon neighboring lands.  Lots shall not be rezoned in a way that is substantially
inconsistent with the uses of the surrounding area, whether more or less restrictive.  The Town
finds and determines that vast acreages of single-use zoning produces uniformity with adverse
consequences, such as traffic congestion, air pollution, and social alienation.  Accordingly, rezonings
may promote mixed uses subject to a high degree of design control.
(C) Suitability as Presently Zoned.  The Hearing Body shall consider the suitability or unsuitability of
the Tract for its use as presently zoned.  This factor, like the others, should be weighed in relation
to the other standards, and instances can exist in which the land may be rezoned to meet public
need, to reflect substantially changed conditions in the neighborhood, or to effectuate important
goals, objectives and policies of the Comprehensive Plan or UDO.
(D) Health, Safety, and Welfare.  The amending ordinance must bear a substantial relationship to the
public health, safety or general welfare, or protect and preserve historical and cultural places and
areas.  The rezoning may be justified, however, if a substantial public need or purpose exists, even
if the private owner of the Tract will also benefit.
(E) Public Policy.  Certain public policies in favor of the rezoning may be considered.  Examples include
a need for affordable housing, economic Development, mixed-use Development, or sustainable
environmental features, which are consistent with neighborhood, area, or specific plans.
(F) Size of Tract.  The Hearing Body shall consider the size, shape, and characteristics of the Tract in
relation to the affected neighboring lands.  Amendatory ordinances shall not rezone a single Lot
when there have been no intervening changes or other saving characteristics.  Proof that a small
Tract is unsuitable for use as zoned, or that there have been substantial changes in the immediate
area, may justify ordinance rezoning.
(G) Other Factors.  The Hearing Body may consider any other factors relevant to the rezoning
application under state law.
Applicant Representations.  Except for rezoning requests submitted in accordance with the provisions 
herein for conditional use district rezonings, the Hearing Body shall not consider any representations 
made by the petitioner that, if the change is granted, the rezoned property will be used for only one of 
the possible range of uses permitted in the requested classification.  Rather, the Hearing Body shall 
consider whether the entire range of permitted uses in the requested classification is more appropriate 
than the range of uses in the existing classification. 
Z-02-20 Forest Creek
June 2020 Town Council
Page 17 of 43
TOWN COUNCIL  
RESOLUTION TO ADOPT A STATEMENT OF CONSISTENCY 
FOR ZONING MAP AMENDMENT APPLICATION  
Z-02-20
WHEREAS, Section 160A-383 of the North Carolina General Statutes specifies that the 
governing board shall, with any ordinance amendment or zoning map amendment decision, 
approve a statement describing whether the action of the governing board is consistent with the 
adopted comprehensive plan.  
WHEREAS, Section 160A-383 of the North Carolina General Statutes specifies that zoning 
regulations shall be made in accordance with a comprehensive plan and prior to adopting or 
rejecting any zoning amendment, the governing board shall adopt one of the following statements, 
which shall not be subject to judicial review:  
(1) A statement approving the zoning amendment and describing its consistency with
an adopted comprehensive plan and explaining why the action taken is reasonable
and in the public interest.
(2) A statement rejecting the zoning amendment and describing its inconsistency with
an adopted comprehensive plan and explaining why the action taken is reasonable
and in the public interest.
(3) A statement approving the zoning amendment and containing at least all of the
following:
a.
A declaration that the approval is also deemed an amendment to the
comprehensive plan. The governing board shall not require any additional
request or application for amendment to the comprehensive plan.
b. An explanation of the change in conditions the governing board took into
account in amending the zoning ordinance to meet the development needs of
the community.
c.
Why the action was reasonable and in the public interest.
WHEREAS, zoning regulations shall be designed to promote the public health, safety, and general 
welfare. The regulations shall be made with reasonable consideration, among other things, as to 
the character of the district and its peculiar suitability for particular uses, and with a view to 
conserving the value of buildings and encouraging the most appropriate use of land throughout the 
Town.  
WHEREAS, the Town Council conducted a public hearing on June 09, 2020 for consideration 
of Zoning Map Amendment application Z-02-20;  
Z-02-20 Forest Creek
June 2020 Town Council
Page 18 of 43
NOW, THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED that the Town Council finds that the Zoning Map 
Amendment application Z-02-20 is reasonable, in the public interest and consistent with the Town 
of Southern Pines Comprehensive Long Range Plan (CLRP) because the proposed RM-2, 
Residential Mixed-Housing, zoning is consistent with the Future Land Use Designation of 
“Residential,” as that term is defined in Chapter 4 of the CLRP.  The proposed rezoning appears 
to be consistent with both the CLRP and Future Land Use Map as well as with many Goals and 
Policies in the CLRP.  Specifically Policy 12, stating that new housing choices foster the provision 
of a mix of housing that meets the financial and physical needs of existing and future residents by 
encouraging development of a variety of housing types in new residential areas and promoting 
compatible infill in existing neighborhoods.  The overall character of the area in which the 
applicant is requesting the RM-2 Residential Mixed Housing zoning will not be negatively 
impacted, nor will the requested zoning result in an inefficient extension of public facilities and 
services because the area is already developed and served by all required facilities. Finally, any 
future redevelopment of the subject property will be required to comply with current site and 
building design requirements, further improving the aesthetics and functionality of the site and 
mitigating potential impacts to neighboring properties and the general public.

Re: Colony 9 CUP Amendment and Rezoning Applications 
 
Dear B.J.: 
 
I represent Colony 9, LLC which is the current owner of certain tracts of land commonly known as 
Sections 1 and 20 within the Forest Creek Golf Club development.  One of the requirements of Colony 9 
when submitting the CUP Amendment and the Rezoning Application to the Town of Southern Pines is to 
identify the Parcel ID number(s) for the Colony 9 property for which the CUP Amendment and the 
Rezoning Application are being made.  When researching that requirement on the Moore County Tax 
Office website, it was determined that a condominium unit located in the Forest Creek Golf Course 
Clubhouse which is owned by James J. Rehak, Jr. and his wife, Mary Kelly Rehak as Trustees for their 
respective Revocable Trusts was acquired by the Trusts by a deed recorded in Book 4931, Page 376 of the 
Moore County Registry a copy of which is attached and had as its PIN # 85730039172.  When locating 
that PIN on the Tax Office’s tax maps, that specific tax map a copy of which is attached shows the 
Rehak’s property including the entirety of the Forest Creek Golf Course Development which is obviously 
an error.   
 
I have also attached a copy of the deed by which Colony 9 acquired a substantial amount of the Forest 
Creek Golf Course Development including the above referenced Sections 1 and 20 as well as a copy of 
the tax map which shows the location of Sections 1 and 20.  Clearly, Colony 9 is the correct owner of 
Sections 1 and 20 as per the tax maps and the condominium unit owned by the Rehaks’ Trusts are located 
within the Clubhouse of the Forest Creek Golf Club and therefore, the tax map reference for PIN # 
85730039172 is in error. 
 
Should you need any additional information, please let me know

FOREST CREEK SECTION 1 AND 20 
REZONING NARRATIVE 
 
The community known as Forest Creek began development in the 1990s and is a gated golf course 
community off Airport Road in Southern Pines, North Carolina.  Two golf courses, a clubhouse, amenities 
and several residential lots and homes have been developed within the property.  In 1999 a Conditional 
Use Permit (CU-04-99) for the RS-3 district was approved which permitted up to a total of 750 residential 
single-family lots to be developed on the property, along with the golf courses and amenity areas.  To 
date, 704 residential lots have been recorded within Forest Creek. 
 
This application seeks to amend the zoning for a portion of the RS-3 district to RM-2 to add multi-family 
condominium development as a potential use for the property. The ability to develop multi-family 
condominiums would only pertain to Sections 1 (+/- 13.36 acres) and 20 (+/- 22.07 acres).   
 
Sections 1 and 20 are located within Forest Creek near the clubhouse and main amenity area, just off 
Meyer Farm Drive.  Potential development of these area would allow for multi-family units or single-family 
detached lots. Sections 1 and 20 were intended to be developed as single-family detached residential 
units.  As the property has developed over the years, a demand for multi-family condominiums has 
surfaced.  The proposed modification to the zoning would allow Colony 9 the ability to offer condominium 
product to the members of the club within the Forest Creek community.  Locating the condominium units 
near the clubhouse, pool and other amenity areas would provide the owners with easy access to the club’s 
recreational features.  
 
These plans are consistent with the Comprehensive Long-Range Plan (CLRP) which designates the 
property as Residential/Golf.  Any condominium buildings would be subject to the Town’s multi-family 
guidelines as specified in the Unified Development Ordinance.  As such, the building elevations and 
materials will be subject to review by the Town Council for an Architectural Compliance Permit. 
 
Water and sewer utilities for Sections 1 and 20 are readily available and were constructed during the 
overall development of Forest Creek.  Any additional infrastructure needed to serve Sections 1 and 20 on-
site will be developed as the parcels are constructed, the cost of which will be by the developer.  Any 
additional on-site utility infrastructure will be located underground. 
 
 
 
Z-02-20 Forest Creek
June 2020 Town Council
Page 22 of 43
EXHIBIT A 
 
Forest Creek Section 1 and 20 
Rezoning Justification  
 
Below are listed the seven (7) criteria required to approve a Zoning Map Amendment application as described in 
Section 2.17.9 of the Town of Southern Pines Unified Development Ordinance (UDO).  Following the individual 
criteria is an explanation, indicated in red, describing how the project demonstrates compliance with each of these 
criteria. 
 
A Zoning Map Amendment is permitted only if the Applicant demonstrates that:  
 
(A) Consistency. Rezoning shall be consistent with the adopted Comprehensive Plan.  
 
The proposed zoning map amendment from RS-3 to RM-2 is consistent with the Comprehensive Long-Range Plan 
(CLRP). The property is currently designated as Residential/Golf. The ability to develop multi‐family condominiums 
would only pertain to Sections 1 (+/‐ 13.36 acres) and 20 (+/‐ 22.07 acres). 
 
The CLRP speaks to future land uses, accommodating growth and maintaining a sustainable mix of land uses, adding 
that the most successful communities and neighborhoods include a compatible, mutually supportive mix of uses in 
order to maintain vital neighborhoods with the ability to accommodate changing housing demands. Development 
of sections 1 and 20 will meet the applicable standards of the UDO. 
 
(B) Adverse Impacts on Neighboring Lands. The Hearing Body shall consider the nature and degree of an adverse 
impact upon neighboring lands. Lots shall not be rezoned in a way that is substantially inconsistent with the uses of 
the surrounding area, whether more or less restrictive. The Town finds and determines that vast acreages of single-
use zoning produces uniformity with adverse consequences, such as traffic congestion, air pollution, and social 
alienation. Accordingly, rezonings may promote mixed uses subject to a high degree of design control.  
 
Proposed development of Sections 1 and 20 will conform to the character of the neighborhood. Buildings will be 
required to meet the internal design standards of Forest Creek. Any residential lots developed in this section will be 
consistent with other lots located near sections 1 and 20. 
 
In addition to internal Forest Creek design standards, multi‐family condominiums will be subject to the Town’s multi‐
family guidelines as specified in the UDO. As such, the building elevations and materials will be subject to review by 
the Town Council for an Architectural Compliance Permit. The conditional zoning will meet the standards and is in 
character with the surrounding properties. 
 
(C) Suitability as Presently Zoned. The Hearing Body shall consider the suitability or unsuitability of the Tract for its 
use as presently zoned. This factor, like the others, should be weighed in relation to the other standards, and 
instances can exist in which the land may be rezoned to meet public need, to reflect substantially changed conditions 
in the neighborhood, or to effectuate important goals, objectives and policies of the Comprehensive Plan or UDO.  
 
As the area continues to grow, there is an increased public need for alternative housing options. The proposed zoning 
would allow Colony 9 the ability to offer additional single‐family detached lots and a condominium product to the 
members of the club within the border of the Forest Creek Golf Community. Locating the condominium units near 
the clubhouse, pool and other amenity areas would provide the owners with easy access to the club’s recreational 
features. 
 
(D) Health, Safety, and Welfare. The amending ordinance must bear a substantial relationship to the public health, 
safety or general welfare, or protect and preserve historical and cultural places and areas. The rezoning may be 
justified, however, if a substantial public need or purpose exists, even if the private owner of the Tract will also 
benefit.  
 
Z-02-20 Forest Creek
June 2020 Town Council
Page 23 of 43
EXHIBIT A 
 
This development will become part of the overall private Forest Creek Golf Community and subject to its standards 
and regulations. The residential neighborhood developed in sections 1 and 20 will continue the existing development 
pattern in the neighborhood and will conform to all development standards of the UDO and engineering 
requirements of the Town. As a result, the use will not be detrimental to or endanger the public health, safety, 
comfort or general welfare of the surrounding neighborhood. 
 
(E) Public Policy. Certain public policies in favor of the rezoning may be considered. Examples include a need for 
affordable housing, economic Development, mixed-use Development, or sustainable environmental features, which 
are consistent with neighborhood, area, or specific plans.  
 
The conditional zoning is compliance with the established development pattern within the existing Forest Creek Golf 
Community. This project is also consistent with the goals and objectives of the Comprehensive Long‐Range Plan and 
establishes a development pattern that is in consistent with the surrounding neighborhood. The development 
pattern also meets the land use goals defined by the CLRP by adding development where public utilities are available 
and developing infill locations, since sections 1 and 20 are located within an established community. 
 
(F) Size of Tract. The Hearing Body shall consider the size, shape, and characteristics of the Tract in relation to the 
affected neighboring lands. Amendatory ordinances shall not rezone a single Lot when there have been no 
intervening changes or other saving characteristics. Proof that a small Tract is unsuitable for use as zoned, or that 
there have been substantial changes in the immediate area, may justify ordinance rezoning.  
 
The ability to develop multi‐family condominiums would only pertain to Sections 1 (+/‐ 13.36 acres) and 20 (+/‐ 22.07 
acres) and will conform to all development standards of the UDO and engineering requirements of the Town. 
 
(G) Other Factors. The Hearing Body may consider any other factors relevant to a rezoning application under state 
law.  
 
The proposed zoning map amendment is limited to Sections 1 and 20.

Agenda Item 
To: 
Reagan Parsons, Town Manager 
Via: 
BJ Grieve, Planning Director 
From: 
Suzy Russell, Planner II 
Subject: 
CU-03-20: Conditional Use Permit; Major Amendment 
to CU-04-99; Increase in Intensity; Designation of 
additional Land Uses; 35.43 Acres;  Applicant, Colony 9, 
LLC Mr. Earl Ellis; Authorized Agent, Mr. Bob Koontz 
of Koontz Jones Design, PLLC.   
Date: 
June 9, 2020 
I.
SUMMARY OF APPLICATION REQUEST:
Mr. Bob Koontz on behalf of Mr. Earl Ellis, of Colony 9, LLC has submitted a Conditional
Use Permit application for a major amendment to Conditional Use Permit CU-04-99
requesting approval to increase the overall total number of residential units permitted, 750
single-family lots, by 25 and also to add a multi-family condominium development as an
allowable use for the property.  The multi-family development would impact sections 1
and 20 in the Forest Creek development and would be limited to a total of 30 units.  The
applicant has also applied separately to rezone section 1 and 20 to RM-2 (Residential
Mixed Housing).  Currently the Forest Creek development is zoned RS-3 (Residential
Single-Family).   Section 1 is 13.36 acres and Section 20 is 22.07 acres.  Section 1 lies east
of Meyer Farm Drive and south of Forest Creek Drive with Section 20 also to the east of
Meyer Farm Drive and north of Forest Creek Drive, within the Forest Creek development
west of the clubhouse.  Infrastructure was constructed during the overall development of
Forest Creek and are readily available presently.  The subject property is identified by the
following: PIN: 857300393172 (PARID 00037691) and the property owner is listed as
Colony 9, LLC.
II.
PLANNING BOARD ACTION:
At the May 21, 2020 Regular Meeting of the Planning Board (held via electronic meeting
due to statewide social distancing requirements), the Planning Board held a legislative
public hearing per UDO §2.5.2 which states that when the Planning Board serves as a
recommending body for an action requiring a quasi-judicial hearing by the Town Council
the Board may follow the rules for a legislative hearing to gather broader public testimony.
The Planning Board heard from those in attendance regarding application CU-03-20.
Planning staff entered staff memo CU-03-20 into the public record as Exhibit A and
presented a review of the Conditional Use Permit application.  The Planning Board

June 2020 Town Council

inquired If people were notified of this CUP application and Ms. Russell responded with 
the following dates: Notice of Planning Board Public Hearing:

o Mailed: May 08, 2020 
o Internet: May 08, 2020 
Mr. BJ, Grieve also responded that over 400 mailed notices went out from the Planning 
Office.   
 
Following staff’s comments, the applicant’s agent, Mr. Bob Koontz presented a series of 
PowerPoint slides, (Exhibit B) summarizing the proposed amendments and addressed 
questions from the Planning Board.   
 
After closing the public hearing, a motion was made by Ms. Diane Westbrook and 
seconded by Mr. Lemuel Dowdy to adopt Attachment A of the staff report as Findings of 
Fact regarding the proposed Conditional Use Permit CU-03-20.  The motion passed 
unanimously 6-0 (Cooper Carter was absent.).  Ms. Diane Westbrook moved to 
recommend to the Town Council approval of Conditional Use Permit CU-01-20 and Ms. 
Kim Wade seconded the motion.  The motion passed unanimously (Cooper Carter was 
absent).    
 
The adopted Planning Board Findings of Fact may be found attached to this staff report.

IV. 
PROJECT DETAILS:  
 
A. Description of Proposed Amendment: 
The applicant submitted a Conditional Use Permit application for a major 
amendment to Conditional Use Permit CU-04-99 requesting approval to increase 
the overall total number of residential units permitted, 750 single-family lots, by 25 
and also to add a multi-family condominium development as a use for the property.  
The multi-family development would impact sections 1 and 20 in the Forest Creek 
development (see Figure 2 above) and would be limited to a total of 30 units.  The 
overall residential family dwelling units will increase to 775 dwelling units, of those 
up to 30 will be multi-family condominiums.  The applicant has applied to rezone 
section 1 and 20 to RM-2 (Residential Mixed Housing).  Currently the Forest Creek 
development is zoned RS-3 (Residential Single-Family).   Sections 1 and 20 were 
previously approved to be used for single-family detached residential units similar 
to the rest of Forest Creek.  Section 1 is 13.36 acres and Section 20 is 22.07 acres.  
Section 1 lies east of Meyer Farm Drive and south of Forest Creek Drive with 
Section 20 also to the east of Meyer Farm Drive and north of Forest Creek Drive, 
within the Forest Creek development west of the clubhouse.  Sewer and water 
infrastructure was constructed during the overall development of Forest Creek and 
is readily available presently (please see Figure 5 above).  Access to the lots will 
be via Meyer Farm Drive, however the applicant has not addressed proposed 
driveway locations at this time.   The applicant has addressed the six (6) criteria  
required for a CUP and provided a narrative for the proposed amendment as well 
as an existing condition plan set showing the location of Section 1 and Section 20 
of Forest Creek and are attached to this staff report.

ii. 
Criteria for Review: 
i. Conditional Use Permit (UDO §2.21.7): 
A conditional Use is permitted only if the applicant demonstrates that: 
A. The proposed conditional use shall comply with all regulations of 
the applicable zoning district and any applicable supplemental use 
regulations; 
B. The proposed conditional use shall conform to the character of the 
neighborhood in which it is located and not injure the use and 
enjoyment of property in the immediate vicinity for the purposes 
already permitted; 
C. Adequate public facilities shall be provided as set forth herein; 
D. The proposed use shall not impede the orderly Development and 
improvement of surrounding property for uses permitted within the 
zoning district or substantially diminish or impair the property 
values within the neighborhood; 
E. The establishment, maintenance, or operation of the proposed use 
shall not be detrimental to or endanger the public health, safety, 
comfort or general welfare; and, 
F. The public interest and welfare supporting the proposed use shall 
be sufficient to outweigh individual interests that are adversely 
affected by the establishment of the proposed use. 
 
iii. 
Staff Comments: 
i. 
General Staff Comments: 
• The applicant is requesting to increase overall density by 25 
dwelling units.  The original approved total number of dwelling 
units approved under CU-04-99 is 750 du.  The total number of 
dwelling units after the request of the applicant is 775 du.  Of the 
total 775 dwelling units 30 may be multi-family condominiums.   
 
• The applicant is requesting to allow multi-family housing for 
Section 1 and Section 20 which are parcels of land that lie within 
the Forest Creek development, an existing gated development.

VII. 
TOWN COUNCIL ACTION: 
 
To either approve or deny a Conditional Use Permit application, the Town Council 
shall make findings of fact and conclusions to the applicable standards. The Town 
Council shall first vote on whether the application is complete and whether the facts 
presented are relevant to the case.  The Town Council shall then vote on whether the 
application complies with the criteria as set forth in Section 2.21.7(A-F) Criteria for 
a Conditional Use Permit, Criteria A-F.  The Town Council may choose one of the 
following motions or any alternative they wish: 
 
I move to: 
 
1. Adopt Attachment “A” of the staff report as our Findings of Fact regarding the 
proposed Conditional Use Permit CU-03-20. 
 
2. Adopt Attachment “A” of the staff report as our Findings of Fact regarding the 
proposed 
Conditional 
Use 
Permit 
CU-03-20 
with 
the 
following 
changes__________________. 
 
Next, the Town Council shall vote on whether to approve, deny or approve with 
conditions the proposed Conditional Use Permit.  The Town Council may choose one 
of the following motions, or any alternative they wish: 
 
I move to : 
 
1. Approve the Conditional Use Permit CU-03-20. 
2. Deny the Conditional Use Permit CU-03-20 
3. Approve the Conditional Use Permit for CU-03-20 with the following additional 
conditions….

ATTACHMENT “A” 
Draft Town Council Findings of Fact 
Conditional Use Permit Application CU-03-20 
 
Finding of Fact #1: 
 
The Town Council finds that the application is complete and that the facts submitted are relevant 
to the case because the request for Conditional Use Permit approval has met the specified submittal 
requirements as required in the Town of Southern Pines UDO Appendices and the evidence 
submitted was sworn testimony by qualified experts or provided through substantiated 
documentation. 
 
Finding of Fact #2: 
 
The Town Council finds that the application complies with UDO §2.21.7 Criteria for a Conditional 
Use Permit, Criteria A-F, in that: 
 
A. The proposed conditional use shall comply with all regulations of the applicable 
zoning district and any applicable supplemental use regulations; 
The Town Council finds that Section 1 and Section 20, two parcels within the Forest Creek 
development will be re-zoned to RM-2 Residential Mixed Housing to allow for up to 30 
condominium multi-family dwelling units to be developed because a Conditional Use 
Permit may be amended, for this request in particular, to designate an additional land use 
under new zoning and increase in intensity under UDO §2.21.13.  Sections 1 and 20 will 
comply with all regulations related to the RM-2 zoning district.       
 
B. The proposed conditional use shall conform to the character of the neighborhood in 
which it is located and not injure the use and enjoyment of property in the immediate 
vicinity for the purposes already permitted;  
The Town Council finds that the proposed multi-family development may be considered 
an appropriate land use inside Forest Creek because it promotes compatible infill in an 
existing neighborhood. The RM-2 multi-family condominium development totaling 35.43 
acres, is limited to Section 1 and Section 20 which lies within the gated community of 
Forest Creek.  The density will only be increased by 25 total dwelling units.     
 
C. Adequate public facilities shall be provided as set forth herein;  
The Town Council finds that adequate facilities are in place and can be extended to serve 
the project.     
  
D. The proposed use shall not impede the orderly development and improvement of 
surrounding property for uses permitted within the zoning district or substantially 
diminish or impair the property values within the neighborhood; 
The Town Council finds the proposed modest increase in density and change in the 
approved Forest Creek CUP to allow multi-family land use in Section 1 and 20 as 
conducive to the community’s long-range goals which encourages development of a 
CU-03-20 Forest Creek
June 2020 Town Council
Page 13 of 24
variety of housing types in new residential areas and promoting compatible infill in existing 
neighborhoods.   
 
E. The establishment, maintenance or operation for the proposed use shall not be 
detrimental to or endanger the public health, safety, comfort, or general welfare; and 
The Town Council finds that the proposed modest increase in density and change in the 
approved Forest Creek CUP to allow multi-family land use in Section 1 and 20 will not 
have detrimental impacts on the safety, comfort or general welfare because future site-
specific development will be required to adhere to all site design standards and building 
standards, including, but not limited to compliance with the building code. The site design 
requirements must be met prior to the Town of Southern Pines approving building permits 
for new commercial and/or multi-family structures.  
 
F. The public interest and welfare supporting the proposed use shall be sufficient to 
outweigh individual interests that are adversely affected by the establishment of the 
proposed use; 
The Town Council finds that the proposed development will comply with applicable 
standards and regulations found within the Town of Southern Pines UDO that are based on 
the public interest and welfare.  The rezoning to RM-2 allowing for 30 multi-family units 
in Section 1 and Section 20 will allow the petitioner the ability to offer the condominium 
dwelling units to the members of the club of Forest Creek.  The proximity of Sections 1 
and 20 to the club’s recreational features support the interest and welfare of the members 
of Forest Creek.

FOREST CREEK SECTION 1 AND 20 
CONDITIONAL USE PERMIT NARRATIVE 
 
The  community  known  as  Forest  Creek  began  development  in  the  1990s  and  is  a  gated  golf  course 
community off Airport Road in Southern Pines, North Carolina.  Two golf courses, a clubhouse, amenities 
and several residential lots and homes have been developed within the property.  In 1999 a Conditional 
Use Permit (CU‐04‐99) for the RS‐3 district was approved which permitted up to a total of 750 residential 
single‐family lots to be developed on the property, along with the golf courses and amenity areas.  To 
date, 704 residential lots have been recorded within Forest Creek. 
 
This application seeks to amend the original Conditional Use Permit (CUP) for the RS‐3 district to increase 
the  overall  total  number  of  residential  units  permitted  by  25  and  add  multi‐family  condominium 
development  as  a  use  for  the  property.    While  the  increase  of  25  units  would  impact  the  overall 
development,  the  ability  to  develop  multi‐family  condominiums  would  only  pertain  to  Sections  1                
(+/‐ 13.36 acres) and 20 (+/‐ 22.07 acres) as shown in the attached exhibit.  Multi‐family development in 
Sections 1 and 20 would be limited to a total of 30 units.   
 
Sections 1 and 20 are located within Forest Creek near the clubhouse and main amenity area, just off 
Meyer Farm Drive.  Potential development of these area would allow for 30 multi‐family units with the 
balance of the property to be developed as 1/3‐acre single‐family detached lots. Sections 1 and 20 were 
intended to be developed as single‐family detached residential units.  As the property has developed over 
the years, a demand for multi‐family condominiums has surfaced.  The proposed modification to the CUP 
would allow Colony 9 the ability to offer the condominium product to the members of the club within the 
Forest Creek community.  Locating the condominium units near the clubhouse, pool and other amenity 
areas would provide the owners with easy access to the club’s recreational features.  
 
These  plans  are  consistent  with  the  Comprehensive  Long‐Range  Plan  (CLRP)  which  designates  the 
property as Residential/Golf.  The condominium buildings would be subject to the Town’s multi‐family 
guidelines  as  specified  in  the  Unified  Development  Ordinance.    As  such,  the  building  elevations  and 
materials will be subject to review by the Town Council for an Architectural Compliance Permit. 
 
Water and sewer utilities for Sections 1 and 20 are readily available and were constructed during the 
overall development of Forest Creek.  Any additional infrastructure needed to serve Sections 1 and 20 on‐
site will be developed as the parcels are constructed, the cost of which will be by the developer.  Any 
additional on‐site utility infrastructure will be located underground. 
 
 
 
CU-03-20 Forest Creek
June 2020 Town Council
Page 19 of 24
EXHIBIT A 
 
Forest Creek Section 1 and 20 
Conditional Use Permit Justification  
 
Below are listed the six (6) criteria required to approve a Conditional Use Permit application as described in Section 
2.21.7 of the Town of Southern Pines Unified Development Ordinance (UDO).  Following the individual criteria is an 
explanation, indicated in red, describing how the project demonstrates compliance with each of these criteria. 
A Conditional Use is permitted only if the Applicant demonstrates that:  
 
(A) The proposed conditional use shall comply with all regulations of the applicable zoning district and any 
applicable supplemental use regulations;  
This application seeks to amend the previously approved Conditional Use Permit ‐ CU‐04‐99 (CUP) for the 
RS‐3 district to increase the overall total number of residential units permitted by 25 and add multi‐family 
condominium development as a use for the property.  While the increase of 25 units would impact the 
overall development, the ability to develop multi‐family condominiums would only pertain to Sections 1 
(+/‐ 13.36 acres) and 20 (+/‐ 22.07 acres) as shown in the attached exhibit.  Multi‐family development in 
Sections 1 and 20 would be limited to a total of 30 units.  Development of sections 1 and 20 will meet the 
applicable standards of the UDO. 
(B) The proposed conditional use shall conform to the character of the neighborhood in which it is located and 
not injure the use and enjoyment of property in the immediate vicinity for the purposes already permitted;  
Proposed development of Sections 1 and 20 will conform to the character of the neighborhood.  Buildings 
will be required to meet the internal design standards of Forest Creek.  Residential lots at 1/3 acre will be 
consistent with other lots located near sections 1 and 20.   
 
In addition to internal Forest Creek design standards, multi‐family condominiums will be subject to the 
Town’s multi‐family guidelines as specified in the UDO.  As such, the building elevations and materials will 
be subject to review by the Town Council for an Architectural Compliance Permit.  The conditional use will 
meet the standards and is in character with the surrounding properties.  
 
(C) Adequate public facilities shall be provided as set forth herein;  
Public water and sewer utilities are readily available for the project and were developed with other sections 
of Forest Creek.  Any cost for on‐site utilities will be borne by the developer. Lots will have adequate access 
to accommodate emergency and waste removal vehicles and any additional utilities to serve residential lots 
or condominiums will be located underground. 
 
(D) The proposed use shall not impede the orderly Development and improvement of surrounding property for 
uses permitted within the zoning district or substantially diminish or impair the property values within the 
neighborhood;  
This project will not impede the development of surrounding properties as it is in conformance with the 
surrounding  development  and  part  of  the  overall  master‐planned  community.    The  proposed  CUP 
modification  would  allow  Colony  9  the  ability  to  offer  additional  single‐family  detached  lots  and  a 
condominium product to the members of the club within the border of the Forest Creek Golf Community.  
Locating the condominium units near the clubhouse, pool and other amenity areas would provide the 
owners with easy access to the club’s recreational features 
 
(E) The establishment, maintenance, or operation of the proposed use shall not be detrimental to or endanger 
the public health, safety, comfort or general welfare; and 
This development will become part of the overall private Forest Creek Golf Community and subject to its 
standards and regulations.  The residential neighborhood developed in sections 1 and 20 will continue the 
existing development pattern in the neighborhood and will conform to all development standards of the 
CU-03-20 Forest Creek
June 2020 Town Council
Page 20 of 24
EXHIBIT A 
 
UDO and engineering requirements of the Town. As a result, the use will not be detrimental to or endanger 
the public health, safety, comfort or general welfare of the surrounding neighborhood. 
 
(F) The public interest and welfare supporting the proposed use shall be sufficient to outweigh individual 
interests that are adversely affected by the establishment of the proposed use. 
The conditional use is in compliance with the established development pattern within the existing Forest 
Creek Golf Community and is in context with the currently approved CUP.  This project is also consistent 
with  the  goals  and  objectives  of  the  Comprehensive  Long‐Range  Plan  and  establishes  a  development 
pattern that is in consistent with the surrounding neighborhood. 
 
The development pattern also meets the land use goals defined by the CLRP by adding development where 
public utilities are available and developing infill locations, since sections 1 and 20 are located within an 
established community.

CAPITAL RESERVE FUND RESOLUTION 
 
 
WHEREAS, there is a need in the Town of Southern Pines to provide funds for future 
capital projects related to its combined water and wastewater system, and WHEREAS, 
NCGS 159-18 authorizes the creation of a capital reserve fund, and WHEREAS, NCGS 
162A, Art. 8 requires that all system development fee proceeds be accounted for in a capital 
reserve fund, the revenue assumptions below reflect an estimate of system development fees 
to be collected over a period of twelve months beginning April 1, 2020: 
 
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the Town Council of Southern Pines that: 
 
 
Section 1: 
The Town Council hereby amends the Capital Reserve Fund -Water for the purpose 
of funding the following capital projects related to the Town’s water system: 
 
 
 
East Morganton Road Water Line Replacement.  An existing 6-inch 
water line will be replaced with a 12-inch water line along East Morganton 
Road from Ridge Street to Valley Road.  This project was initiated in FY19-
20 and is scheduled for completion in FY 20-21.  The cost estimate for the 
project is $378,340.  The Town intends to appropriate approximately 
$175,928 of System Development Fee revenues to the CRF for this purpose 
with the balance of upfront costs covered by water capital funds and 
remaining Impact Fees collected prior to October 1, 2018.  The project will 
address future infill development while reducing areas of low fire flow along 
Morganton Road, south of Weymouth Woods. 
 
 
 
 
 
 
The 2020-2021 appropriation from the budget ordinance to the CRF-
Water of SDF proceeds for this purpose is $175,928 
 
Pennsylvania Avenue/Pee Dee Road Water Line Replacement.  An 
existing 10-inch water line will be replaced with a 16-inch water line along 
Pennsylvania/Pee Dee Road from Connecticut Avenue to Central Drive.  
This project was implemented in 2019 and is estimated to cost $1,453,034.  
The Town intends to appropriate approximately $228,853 of System 
Development Fee revenues to the CRF for this purpose with the balance of 
upfront costs covered by water capital funds and remaining Impact Fees 
collected prior to October 1, 2018.  The project will address future growth, 
pressure, and flow rates to the northern portion of Town and in particular the 
proposed North Elevated Storage Tank. 
 
 
 
2018 thru 2020 appropriations to the CCRF-Water of SDF proceeds 
for this purpose are hereby amended from $330,000 to $228,853 
 
Midland Road Water Line Replacement.  An existing 6-inch and 8-inch 
water line will be replaced with a 12-inch water line along Midland Road 
from Knoll Road to Pee Dee Road.  This project is scheduled for 
implementation in 2023 and is estimated to cost $1,069,011.  The Town 
intends to appropriate approximately $136,299 of System Development Fee 
revenues to the CRF for this purpose with the balance of upfront costs 
covered by water capital funds and remaining Impact Fees collected prior to 
October 1, 2018.  The project will address future growth and pressures to 
anticipated further development in the Mid-South and Talamore areas. 
 
 
 
The 2020-2021 appropriation from the budget ordinance to the CRF-
Water of SDF proceeds for this purpose is $71,861 
 
 
North Pressure Zone.  The Town plans to install a 184 ft. high 1.0 MG 
North Elevated Storage Tank and associated valves.  This project is 
scheduled for implementation in 2023 and is estimated to cost 
$3,212,308.  The Town intends to appropriate approximately 
$1,204,616 of System Development Fee revenues to the CRF for this 
purpose with the balance of upfront costs covered by water capital 
funds and installment loans.  The project will successfully add a 
pressure zone in the northern portion of our service area to address 
potential low flow conditions which could impact future growth in 
this area. 
 
 
 
The 2020-2021 appropriation from the budget ordinance to the CRF-
Water of SDF proceeds for this purpose is $0 
 
 
US 1 Booster Pump Addition.  The Town plans to install infrastructure to 
provide for an additional 4,500 gpm Pumping Capacity to the US 1 
Booster Pump Station.  This project is scheduled for implementation 
in 2025 and is estimated to cost $675,184.  The Town intends to 
appropriate approximately $40,511 of System Development Fee 
revenues to the CRF for this purpose with the balance of upfront 
costs covered by water capital funds and potentially loans.  The 
additional flow will support ongoing development throughout our 
Water service area. 
 
 
 
The 2020-2021 appropriation from the budget ordinance to the CRF 
of SDF proceeds for this purpose is $0 
 
 
Section 2: 
The Town Council hereby amends the Capital Reserve Fund- Sewer for the purpose 
of funding the following capital projects related to the Town’s wastewater system: 
 
 
 
 
 
Warrior Woods Pump Station Improvements:  Significant upgrades to 
both the Warrior Woods Pump Station and associated Force Main will occur through 
a series of projects that are ultimately scheduled for completion in 2027. The 
estimated cost of all projects is $8,215,965.  The Town intends to appropriate 
approximately $2,834,508 of System Development Fee revenues to the CRF for this 
purpose with the balance derived from Retained Earnings, Sewer Capital Funds, and 
remaining Impact Fees collected prior to October 1, 2018.  The first phase of this 
project was initiated in FY 2018-2019 with completion in 2020 with $791,250 
appropriated in the 2018-2019 Budget from the previous Impact Fee account and 
$263,750 appropriated from Sewer Capital Funds.  Previously, $213,827 has been 
appropriated to the CRF-Wastewater SDF toward this multi-phased project.  The 
upgrades will address additional capacity needed to support further development 
within all wastewater infrastructure in addition to replacing the maintenance heavy 
current facilities. 
 
 
 
The 2020-2021 appropriation from the budget ordinance to the CRF-
Wastewater of SDF proceeds for this purpose is $174,865 
 
 
Section 3: 
These Capital Reserve Funds shall remain effective until all the above listed 
projects, and any projects added in the future, are completed.  Capital Reserve Funds 
may be amended by the Town Council as needed to add additional appropriations, 
modify or eliminate existing capital projects, and/or add new capital projects. 
 
Section 4: 
This resolution becomes effective July 1, 2020. 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
I certify that this resolution was adopted by the Town Council of the Town of Southern Pines at 
its meeting of June 22nd, 2020 as shown in the minutes of the Town Council for that date. 
 
 
 
_________________________________ 
Peggy K. Smith, Town Clerk

follows:

ordinance amendment.

under subsection (b) of this section.

(2) Bulk water rate calculations. 
(a)   Contract amount.  The contract amount will be for any quantity equal to or greater 
than 50,000 gallons per day. 
(b)   Minimum take or pay.  The customer must take or pay for the annual minimum stated 
in the contract. 
(c)   Usage over contract amount. The customer may use an amount greater than the 
contract amount when capacity is available, and the customer has obtained prior permission 
from the town. 
(d)   Annual adjustment to contract amount.  The contract provisions may be modified or 
altered by mutual written agreement of the parties. 
(e)   Flat rate charge.  The contract will provide for a flat rate charge, based on per 1,000 
gallons purchased, with a minimum total payout. 
(f)   Rate adjustments.  The town will adjust the rate, same percentage, per 1,000 gallons 
sold to the purchaser as it does to its regular, in-town, paying customers. The rate charge 
shall become effective in the July billing each year. 
(B) Sewer Rates.  These charges will be reviewed annually and adjusted as necessary via an 
ordinance amendment.

follows:

      (2)   The Town may waive sewerage charges for: 
         (a)   Water customers who are not connected to a public sewer system; or 
         (b)   Water customers who use water provided by the Town for purposes that do not result in 
discharge to a public sewer system, if the customer provides a separate meter for such water to 
which standard water rates apply, including minimum and connection fees. 
      (3)   Sewer service for customers utilizing well water, but desiring sewerage service, must

be afforded Town employees to inspect.

APPROVED AS TO FORM:
